Kafalah — Surety
beginner
8 min
Kafalah: Definition, Evidence, and Two Types
Definitional and foundational text on kafalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of kafalah, distinguish it from hawalah, cite the Quranic evidence for its validity, identify the four technical terms, and classify the two types (kafalah bil nafs and kafalah bil mal).

Core Idea
Kafalah creates joint liability: both debtor and guarantor are equally responsible.

This lesson introduces the Hanafi concept of kafalah (suretyship/guarantee). You will learn the meaning of kafalah, how it differs from hawalah (transfer of debt), the four key parties and object, and the two main types: guarantee of a person (kafalah bil nafs) and guarantee of property (kafalah bil mal). The Quranic evidence from Surah Yusuf and Surah Al Imran establishes its permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the core meaning of kafalah
Read the necessary note: kafalah means assuming responsibility for a debt or person. Both the principal debtor and the guarantor (kafil) are liable; the creditor can claim from either.
Contrast with hawalah where liability shifts entirely.
2
Learn the Quranic evidence
Two verses: Surah Yusuf 12:72 (word 'za'em' meaning guarantor) and Surah Al Imran 3:37 (Zakariya sponsors Maryam). Understand how these prove the permissibility of kafalah.
The dalil is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah in this context.
3
Memorize the four technical terms
Kafil (guarantor), Makful 'anhu (principal debtor), Makful lahu (creditor), Makful bihi (the object: debt or person).
These terms are foundational for all kafalah transactions.
4
Distinguish the two types
Kafalah bil nafs: guarantee to produce a person in court. Kafalah bil mal: guarantee to pay a debt. Both are permissible.
The object (makful bihi) determines the type.

كتاب الكفالة )
ضروری نوٹ كفالہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مثلا زید پر قرض ہے تو میں اس کے قرض کا زمہ دار ہوں، وہ نہیں دے گا تو میں دوں گا۔ کفالت کی صورت میں دونوں آدمی قرض ادا کرنے کے ذمہ دار ہوتے ہیں۔ اور قرض دینے والا دونوں میں سے کسی ایک سے قرض وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ اس کے قریب قریب حوالہ ہے۔ اس میں یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اصل مدیون اب قرض ادا نہیں کرے گا۔ اس کے بدلے اب صرف میں قرض ادا کروں گا۔ اس صورت میں قرض دینے والا صرف ذمہ دار سے قرض وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ کفالت صیح ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ قالوا نفقد صواع الملك ولمن جاء به حمل بغیر وانا به زعيم (الف) (آیت ۷۲ سورۃ یوسف (۱۲) اس آیت میں زعيم کا لفظ ہے جس کے معنی ذمہ دار اور کفیل کے ہیں۔ آیت کا مطلب ہے کہ جو بادشاہ کا پیالہ لادے گا اس کو ایک اونٹ کا بوجھ ملے گا اور میں اس کا كفيل ہوں۔ اس سے كفالت كا ثبوت ہوا۔ حضرت مریم علیہا السلام کے بارے میں ہے۔ وكفلها زكريا (ب) ( آیت ۳۷ سوره آل عمران ۳) که ذکریا علیہ السلام نے حضرت مریم کی کفالت لی۔ اس سے کفالت کا ثبوت ہوا۔ كفالت میں چار الفاظ ہیں (۱) كفیل : جو خود ذمہ دار بنا ، ضامن، اس کو زعيم اور تحمیل بھی کہتے ہیں (۲) مکفول عنہ: مقروض جس کی جانب سے قرض ادا کرنے کی ذمہ داری کفیل لے رہا ہے (۳) مکفول لہ: قرض دینے والا ، جس کے لئے كفیل بن رہا ہے (۴) مکفول بہ: وہ مال جس کے ادا کرنے کا كفیل بن رہا ہے، یاوہ آدمی جس کو مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنے کیذ مہ داری لے رہا ہے کہ ابھی اس کو ضمانت پر چھوڑ دیں۔ وقت مقررہ پر اس کو میں مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنے کا ذمہ دار ہوں بشرطیکہ وہ زندہ ہو۔
[۱۴۱۸) (۱) كفالہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں، كفالہ بالنفس اور كفالہ بالمال۔
كفالت کی قسمیں: کفالت کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ كفالہ بالنفس اور كفالہ بالمال۔ كفالہ بالنفس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فلاں آدمی مجلس قضاء میں مقدمہ کے لئے مطلوب ہے اس کو ابھی چھوڑ دیں، میں اس کو وقت مقررہ پر مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنے کا ذمہ دار ہوں۔ اس کو كفالہ بالنفس کہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ ذات اور نفس حاضر کرنے کا كفیل بنا۔
دوسرا ہے كفالہ بالمال : اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فلاں آدمی پر اتنا قرض ہے اس کو ادا کرنے کا میں كفیل اور ذمہ دار ہوں ، وہ ادا نہیں کرے گا تو میں اس قرض کو ادا کر دوں گا۔ اس کو كفالہ بالمال کہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ مال ادا کرنے کی ذمہ داری لے رہا ہے۔
۱۴۱۹) (۲) پس كفالہ بالنفس جائز ہے اور اس کی ذمہ داری مکفول یہ کو حاضر کرتا ہے۔
ت كفالہ بالنفس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مکفول سہ یعنی جس کی ذمہ داری لی ہے اس کو مقررہ وقت میں مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنا ہے۔ اس کا حاشیہ : (الف) ہم لوگ بادشاہ کا پیالہ کم پاتے ہیں۔ اور جو اس کو لائے گا اس کو ایک اونٹ مال ملے گا اور میں اس کا كفيل ہوں (ب ) حضرت ذکر يا حضرت مریم کے
كفيل بنے۔
Book of Kafalah. [18] (1) 1318 (1) Kafalah is of two types: kafalah bil nafs and kafalah bil mal. [1419] (2) So kafalah bil nafs... (necessary note: The meaning of kafalah is, for example, Zaid has a debt, so I am responsible for his debt; if he does not pay, I will pay. In the case of kafalah, both persons are responsible for paying the debt, and the lender can collect from either. Close to it is hawalah, where the original debtor will no longer pay; instead only I will pay. In that case the lender can only collect from the responsible party. The evidence for the validity of kafalah is this verse: 'They said: We miss the king's cup. For whoever brings it, a camel-load (reward), and I am its guarantor.' (Surah Yusuf 72). In this verse is the word 'za'em' which means responsible and guarantor. The meaning of the verse is that whoever brings the king's cup will get a camel-load, and I am its guarantor. From this kafalah is proven. Regarding Maryam (peace be upon her), it is said: 'And Zakariya sponsored her' (Surah Al Imran 37). That Zakariya (peace be upon him) took sponsorship of Maryam. From this kafalah is proven. In kafalah there are four terms: (1) Kafil: the one who makes himself responsible; the guarantor; also called za'em and tahammul. (2) Makful 'anhu: the debtor on whose behalf the kafil takes responsibility to pay. (3) Makful lahu: the lender for whom the kafil becomes guarantor. (4) Makful bihi: the property for which he becomes guarantor, or the person whom he guarantees to produce in the court; that is, now release him on bail; I am responsible to produce him in court at the appointed time, provided he is alive. [1418] (1) Kafalah has two types: kafalah bil nafs and kafalah bil mal. Types of kafalah: There are two types. Kafalah bil nafs means that a certain person is required in court for a case; release him now; I am responsible to produce him at the appointed time. This is called kafalah bil nafs because he becomes guarantor for producing the person (self). The second is kafalah bil mal: It means that a person has a certain debt; I become guarantor and responsible to pay it; if he does not pay, I will pay the debt. This is called kafalah bil mal because he takes responsibility to pay the property. [1419] (2) So kafalah bil nafs is permissible, and its responsibility is to produce the makful (the one guaranteed). That is, kafalah bil nafs means to produce the makful 'anhu (the one on whose behalf responsibility is taken) in court at the appointed time. Its footnote: (a) 'We find the king's cup; and whoever brings it will get a camel-load and I am its guarantor.' (b) Zakariya became the guarantor (sponsor) of Maryam.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This opening passage from the Book of Kafalah (Suretyship/Guarantee) defines the topic, presents its legal evidence, and outlines its two main types. The passage is a definitional and foundational text (memorization anchor). First, a necessary note clarifies the meaning of kafalah: if someone owes a debt, a kafil (guarantor) assumes responsibility; both the original debtor and the kafil are liable, and the creditor can claim from either. This is distinguished from hawalah (transfer of debt) where liability shifts entirely to the transferee. The evidence for kafalah's validity is derived from the Quranic verse in Surah Yusuf (12:72) where the word 'za'em' (guarantor) appears, and from the story of Zakariya sponsoring Maryam (Surah Al Imran 3:37). The passage then enumerates the four technical terms: kafil (guarantor), makful 'anhu (the principal debtor), makful lahu (the creditor), and makful bihi (either the debt or the person to be produced in court). Finally, it categorizes kafalah into two types: kafalah bil nafs (guarantee of the person, i.e., producing someone in court) and kafalah bil mal (guarantee of property, i.e., paying a debt). Kafalah bil nafs is declared permissible (ja'iz).

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): A contract of guarantee where a person assumes responsibility for a debt or for producing a person in court.
كفیل (kafil): The guarantor who undertakes the obligation; also called ضامن and زعيم.
مکفول عنہ (makful 'anhu): The principal debtor on whose behalf the guarantee is given.
مکفول لہ (makful lahu): The creditor in whose favor the guarantee is given.
مکفول بہ (makful bihi): The object of guarantee: either a debt (money) or a person to be produced in court.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary difference between kafalah and hawalah?
A) In kafalah, the creditor can claim from both the original debtor and the guarantor; in hawalah, only from the transferee.
B) In kafalah, only the guarantor is liable; in hawalah, both are liable.
C) Kafalah is only for property; hawalah is for persons.
D) Kafalah requires a written contract; hawalah does not.

Key Takeaway
Kafalah is a permissible contract of guarantee with two types: personal surety (bil nafs) and property surety (bil mal), established by Quranic evidence and distinguished from hawalah by joint liability.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate

Kafalah bil-Nafs: Definition and Proofs
Definition and proof of kafalah bil-nafs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two types of kafalah, explain the Hanafi ruling on kafalah bil-nafs, and cite the primary textual proofs (Quran, hadith, and athar) that establish its validity.

Core Idea
Kafalah bil-nafs is permissible because the guarantor has the ability to produce the person, proven by Quran, Sunnah, and practice of the Sahaba.

This lesson introduces the concept of kafalah (suretyship) and focuses on kafalah bil-nafs (suretyship for the person). We will examine its definition, its permissibility in the Hanafi school, and the textual proofs that establish its validity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of kafalah
The passage begins by stating that kafalah is of two types: kafalah bil-nafs and kafalah bil-mal. Note the distinction: one for the person, one for property.
This is a standard classification in the Hanafi school.
2
State the ruling of kafalah bil-nafs
The text explicitly says: 'فالكفالة بالنفس جائزة' (kafalah bil-nafs is permissible). The content of this guarantee is the production of the guaranteed person (إحضار المكفول به).
The ruling is ja'iz (permissible) and binding once contracted.
3
Review the Quranic proofs
Two verses are cited: Surah Yusuf (72) with the word 'za'im' (guarantor) and Surah Al Imran (37) with 'wa kafalaha Zakariyya'. Explain how each word indicates kafalah.
The word 'za'im' is synonymous with kafil; 'kafalaha' is a verb form.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith 'al-za'im gharim' (the guarantor is responsible) is presented as a general proof covering both types of kafalah.
This hadith is narrated by Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi.
5
Consider the athar (Companion reports)
Two reports: Umar taking sureties for a person, and Abdullah ibn Mas'ud taking sureties for apostates. Also Hammad's statement that if the guaranteed person dies, the guarantor has no liability.
These athar show the practice of the Sahaba, reinforcing the ruling.

Source Text

كتاب الكفالة
الكفالة ضربان: كفالة بالنفس وكفالة بالمال.
فالكفالة بالنفس جائزة والمضمون بها إحضار المكفول به.
وتنعقد إذا قال: تكفلت بنفس فلان أو برقبته أو بروحه أو بجسده أو برأسه أو بنصفه أو بثلثه.
ضروری نوٹ: کفالہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مثلا زید پر قرض ہے تو میں اس کے قرض کا زمہ دار ہوں، وہ نہیں دے گا تو میں دوں گا۔ کفالت کی صورت میں دونوں آدمی قرض ادا کرنے کے ذمہ دار ہوتے ہیں۔ اور قرض دینے والا دونوں میں سے کسی ایک سے قرض وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ اس کے قریب قریب حوالہ ہے۔ اس میں یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اصل مدیون اب قرض ادا نہیں کرے گا۔ اس کے بدلے اب صرف میں قرض ادا کروں گا۔ اس صورت میں قرض دینے والا صرف ذمہ دار سے قرض وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ کفالت صحیح ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ قالوا نفقد صواع الملك ولمن جاء به حمل بغير وانا به زعيم (آیت ۷۲ سورۃ یوسف). اس آیت میں زعیم کا لفظ ہے جس کے معنی ذمہ دار اور کفیل کے ہیں۔ آیت کا مطلب ہے کہ جو بادشاہ کا پیالہ لادے گا اس کو ایک اونٹ کا بوجھ ملے گا اور میں اس کا کفیل ہوں۔ اس سے کفالت کا ثبوت ہوا۔ حضرت مریم علیہا السلام کے بارے میں ہے: وكفلها زكريا (آیت ۳۷ سوره آل عمران). کہ ذکریا علیہ السلام نے حضرت مریم کی کفالت لی۔ اس سے کفالت کا ثبوت ہوا۔ کفالت میں چار الفاظ ہیں: (۱) کفیل: جو خود ذمہ دار بنا، ضامن، اس کو زعیم اور تحمیل بھی کہتے ہیں (۲) مکفول عنہ: مقروض جس کی جانب سے قرض ادا کرنے کی ذمہ داری کفیل لے رہا ہے (۳) مکفول لہ: قرض دینے والا، جس کے لئے کفیل بن رہا ہے (۴) مکفول بہ: وہ مال جس کے ادا کرنے کا کفیل بن رہا ہے، یا وہ آدمی جس کو مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنے کی ذمہ داری لے رہا ہے کہ ابھی اس کو ضمانت پر چھوڑ دیں۔ وقت مقررہ پر اس کو میں مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنے کا ذمہ دار ہوں بشرطیکہ وہ زندہ ہو۔
كفالہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں، كفالہ بالنفس اور كفالہ بالمال۔
كفالہ بالنفس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فلاں آدمی مجلس قضاء میں مقدمہ کے لئے مطلوب ہے اس کو ابھی چھوڑ دیں، میں اس کو وقت مقررہ پر مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنے کا ذمہ دار ہوں۔ اس کو كفالہ بالنفس کہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ ذات اور نفس حاضر کرنے کا کفیل بنا۔
دوسرا ہے كفالہ بالمال: اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فلاں آدمی پر اتنا قرض ہے اس کو ادا کرنے کا میں کفیل اور ذمہ دار ہوں، وہ ادا نہیں کرے گا تو میں اس قرض کو ادا کر دوں گا۔ اس کو كفالہ بالمال کہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ مال ادا کرنے کی ذمہ داری لے رہا ہے۔
پس كفالہ بالنفس جائز ہے اور اس کی ذمہ داری مکفول بہ کو حاضر کرتا ہے۔
كفالہ بالنفس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مکفول بہ یعنی جس کی ذمہ داری لی ہے اس کو مقررہ وقت میں مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل حدیث ہے: سمعت أبا أمامة قال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: العارية مؤداة والمنحة مردودة والدين مقضى والزعيم غارم (أبو داود، الترمذي). اس حدیث میں الزعیم غارم ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کفیل ذمہ دار ہے۔ اور اس میں دونوں قسم کے کفیل شامل ہو سکتے ہیں كفیل بالنفس بھی اور كفیل بالمال بھی۔ اس سے كفالہ بالنفس کا ثبوت ہوا۔
اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے حمزہ بن عمرو الاسلمی کو مصدقا بھیجا، فوقع رجل على جارية امرأته فاخذ حمزة من الرجل كفلاء حتى قدم على عمر وكان عمر قد جلده مأة جلدة فصدقهم وعذرهم بالجهالة۔ اور جریر والاشعث لعبد الله بن مسعود في المرتدين استتابهم وكفلهم فتابوا وكفلهم عشائرهم۔ وقال حماد: إذا تكفل بنفس فمات فلا شيء عليه۔ ان دونوں اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ كفالہ بالنفس لینا جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دوسرے کی ذات پر کفیل کا بس نہیں چلے گا اس لئے كفالہ بالنفس لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ دوسرے کو حاضر کرنے کی استطاعت تو ہے اس لئے كفالہ بالنفس جائز ہے۔
كفالہ بالنفس منعقد ہوتا ہے اگر کہے: میں فلاں کی جان کا كفیل بنا، یا اس کی گردن کا، یا اس کی روح، یا اس کے جسم، یا اس کے سر، یا اس کے آدھے کا، یا اس کی تہائی کا كفیل ہوں۔ قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ لفظ جس سے پورا انسان مراد ہوتا ہو ان الفاظ سے كفالہ بالنفس ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا نفس سے پورا انسان مراد ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح گردن بولنے سے پورا انسان مراد لیتے ہیں۔ اسی طرح روح جسم اور سر سے پورا انسان مراد لیتے ہیں۔ اور آدھا اور تہائی کا لفظ پورے انسان میں شائع ہوتے ہیں اس لئے ان لفظوں سے بھی پورا انسان مراد ہوگا اور كفالہ بالنفس ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
Book of Kafalah. Kafalah is of two types: kafalah for the person and kafalah for property. Kafalah for the person is permissible, and what is guaranteed by it is the production of the guaranteed person. It is contracted when he says: 'I guarantee the person of so-and-so' or 'his neck' or 'his soul' or 'his body' or 'his head' or 'half of him' or 'a third of him.' [Urdu commentary: Necessary note: The meaning of kafalah is, for example, Zaid has a debt, so I am responsible for his debt; if he does not pay, I will pay. In the case of kafalah, both people are responsible for paying the debt, and the creditor can collect from either of them. Close to it is hawalah. In that, the original debtor will no longer pay the debt; instead, only I will pay. In that case, the creditor can only collect from the responsible person. The proof for the validity of kafalah is the verse: 'They said: We miss the king's cup, and for whoever brings it is a camel-load, and I am its guarantor.' (Surah Yusuf 72). In this verse is the word za'im, which means responsible and guarantor. The meaning is that whoever brings the king's cup will get a camel-load, and I am its guarantor. This proves kafalah. Regarding Maryam, peace be upon her: 'And Zakariyya guaranteed her' (Surah Al Imran 37). This proves kafalah. There are four terms in kafalah: (1) kafil: he who makes himself responsible, also called dhamin, za'im, and tahammul; (2) makful 'anhu: the debtor on whose behalf the kafil takes responsibility; (3) makful lahu: the creditor for whom the kafil becomes responsible; (4) makful bihi: the property for which he becomes responsible, or the person whom he undertakes to produce in the court, that he be released on bail, and he undertakes to produce him at the appointed time in court, provided he is alive. Kafalah is of two types: kafalah bi al-nafs and kafalah bi al-mal. Kafalah bi al-nafs means that a certain person is required in court for a case; let him go now, and I am responsible for producing him at the appointed time in court. This is called kafalah bi al-nafs because he becomes the guarantor for the person and self. The second is kafalah bi al-mal: meaning that a certain person has a debt of such amount, I am his guarantor and responsible; if he does not pay, I will pay the debt. This is called kafalah bi al-mal because he takes responsibility for paying the property. So kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible and its responsibility is to produce the makful bihi. The meaning of kafalah bi al-nafs is to produce the makful bihi, i.e., the one for whom responsibility is taken, at the appointed time in court. Its proof is the hadith: I heard Abu Umamah say: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: 'The borrowed item is to be returned, the gift is to be given back, the debt is to be paid, and the guarantor is responsible.' (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi). In this hadith, 'al-za'im gharim' means that the guarantor is responsible. And this includes both types of guarantors: the guarantor for the person and the guarantor for property. Thus kafalah bi al-nafs is proven. There is also evidence in the athar that Umar sent Hamzah ibn 'Amr al-Aslami as a collector, then a man fell upon the slave-girl of his wife, so Hamzah took guarantors for the person from the man until he came to Umar, and Umar had flogged him one hundred lashes; he affirmed them and excused them due to ignorance. And Jarir and al-Ash'ath to 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud regarding the apostates: they made them repent and took sureties for them, so they repented and their tribes gave sureties for them. And Hammad said: If one becomes a guarantor for a person and then the guaranteed person dies, there is nothing upon him. From these two athar, it is known that taking kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible. Imam Shafi'i says that a guarantor has no control over another's person, therefore kafalah bi al-nafs is not permissible. We say that one does have the ability to produce the other, therefore kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible. Kafalah bi al-nafs is contracted if he says: I become a guarantor for the life of so-and-so, or for his neck, or his soul, or his body, or his head, or half of him, or a third of him. The rule is that any word that refers to the entire person constitutes kafalah bi al-nafs. For example, by 'nafs' the entire person is meant. Similarly, by saying 'neck' the entire person is meant. Likewise, by 'soul', 'body', and 'head' the entire person is meant. And the words 'half' and 'third' are spread over the entire person, so by these words also the entire person is intended, and kafalah bi al-nafs is established.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the book of Kafalah. The author first defines kafalah as having two types: kafalah bil-nafs (suretyship for the person) and kafalah bil-mal (suretyship for property). He then states the ruling that kafalah bil-nafs is permissible (ja'iz), and its content is the production (ihdar) of the guaranteed person (makful bihi) in court. The contracting of kafalah bil-nafs occurs through specific verbal formulas that refer to the whole person: by saying 'I guarantee the person of so-and-so' or 'his neck', 'his soul', 'his body', 'his head', 'half of him', or 'a third of him'. 

The commentary provides the legal proofs. First, the Quranic verse from Surah Yusuf (72) where the word 'za'im' is used, meaning guarantor. This proves the general validity of kafalah. Second, the verse about Maryam 'wa kafalaha Zakariyya' shows kafalah in action. Then the hadith 'al-za'im gharim' (the guarantor is responsible) from Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi directly establishes that a guarantor is liable, which includes both types. Additionally, reports from the Sahaba (athar) show that the Companions practiced kafalah bil-nafs: Hamzah took sureties for a person, and Ibn Mas'ud took sureties for apostates. Hammad's statement that if the guaranteed person dies, the guarantor has no liability shows the limited scope of kafalah bil-nafs. 

The passage also includes a dispute with Imam Shafi'i, who held kafalah bil-nafs invalid because one cannot guarantee another's person (lack of control). The Hanafi response is that one does have istita'ah (ability) to produce the person, as seen in the athar. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that it is permissible. 

The contracting formula is explained by the maxim that any word implying the whole person makes kafalah bil-nafs valid. This includes direct references (nafs, raqaba, ruh, jasad, ra's) and fractional parts (nisf, thulth) because they are considered to encompass the whole person in this context.

Key Terms
الكفالة (al-kafalah): A contract where one person (kafil) assumes responsibility for another's debt or personal appearance.
كفالة بالنفس (kafalah bi al-nafs): Suretyship for the person: the kafil undertakes to produce a specific person (makful bihi) at a given time and place.
كفالة بالمال (kafalah bi al-mal): Suretyship for property: the kafil undertakes to pay a debt or deliver a specific property if the principal debtor fails.
زعيم (za'im): Guarantor, surety; one who takes responsibility for another's obligation.
مكفول به (makful bihi): The object of the guarantee: either the property (debt) or the person to be produced.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is NOT a proof for the permissibility of kafalah bil-nafs?
A) The verse 'wa ana bihi za'im' (Surah Yusuf 72)
B) The verse 'wa kafalaha Zakariyya' (Surah Al Imran 37)
C) The hadith 'al-za'im gharim'
D) The principle of istihsan

Key Takeaway
Kafalah bil-nafs is permissible in the Hanafi school, supported by Quran, hadith, and the practice of the Sahaba, and it is binding once contracted.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Kafalah bil-Nafs: The Shafi'i Dispute and Contracting Formulas
Dispute with Shafi'i and contracting formulas for kafalah bil-nafs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Shafi'i objection to kafalah bil-nafs, articulate the Hanafi response, and identify valid expressions for contracting kafalah bil-nafs.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school validates kafalah bil-nafs because it is a promise to produce, not control, and any word implying the whole person suffices.

This lesson addresses the inter-madhhab dispute regarding kafalah bil-nafs and details the specific verbal formulas that constitute a valid contract of suretyship for the person in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
State the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that kafalah bil-nafs is invalid because a guarantor cannot control another's person. The objection is based on lack of dominion over another's freedom.
2
Present the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds by pointing to istita'ah (ability) to produce the person, not control. The athar (practice of the Sahaba) demonstrate that taking sureties for persons was practiced.
The text says: 'We say that one does have the ability to produce the other, therefore kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible.'
3
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference is that Hanafis allow bail bonds to ensure a defendant appears in court, while Shafi'is do not recognize such a contract as valid.
4
List the valid expressions
The passage lists seven expressions that constitute kafalah bil-nafs: nafs (person), raqaba (neck), ruh (soul), jasad (body), ra's (head), nisf (half), thulth (third).
5
Understand the underlying principle
The rule is that any word that refers to the entire person (or is considered to do so in this context) makes the kafalah valid. Even fractional terms like 'half' or 'third' are interpreted as referring to the whole person.
The text explains: 'the words 'half' and 'third' are spread over the entire person, so by these words also the entire person is intended.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الكفالة
الكفالة ضربان: كفالة بالنفس وكفالة بالمال.
فالكفالة بالنفس جائزة والمضمون بها إحضار المكفول به.
وتنعقد إذا قال: تكفلت بنفس فلان أو برقبته أو بروحه أو بجسده أو برأسه أو بنصفه أو بثلثه.
ضروری نوٹ: کفالہ کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مثلا زید پر قرض ہے تو میں اس کے قرض کا زمہ دار ہوں، وہ نہیں دے گا تو میں دوں گا۔ کفالت کی صورت میں دونوں آدمی قرض ادا کرنے کے ذمہ دار ہوتے ہیں۔ اور قرض دینے والا دونوں میں سے کسی ایک سے قرض وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ اس کے قریب قریب حوالہ ہے۔ اس میں یہ ہوتا ہے کہ اصل مدیون اب قرض ادا نہیں کرے گا۔ اس کے بدلے اب صرف میں قرض ادا کروں گا۔ اس صورت میں قرض دینے والا صرف ذمہ دار سے قرض وصول کر سکتا ہے۔ کفالت صحیح ہونے کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ قالوا نفقد صواع الملك ولمن جاء به حمل بغير وانا به زعيم (آیت ۷۲ سورۃ یوسف). اس آیت میں زعیم کا لفظ ہے جس کے معنی ذمہ دار اور کفیل کے ہیں۔ آیت کا مطلب ہے کہ جو بادشاہ کا پیالہ لادے گا اس کو ایک اونٹ کا بوجھ ملے گا اور میں اس کا کفیل ہوں۔ اس سے کفالت کا ثبوت ہوا۔ حضرت مریم علیہا السلام کے بارے میں ہے: وكفلها زكريا (آیت ۳۷ سوره آل عمران). کہ ذکریا علیہ السلام نے حضرت مریم کی کفالت لی۔ اس سے کفالت کا ثبوت ہوا۔ کفالت میں چار الفاظ ہیں: (۱) کفیل: جو خود ذمہ دار بنا، ضامن، اس کو زعیم اور تحمیل بھی کہتے ہیں (۲) مکفول عنہ: مقروض جس کی جانب سے قرض ادا کرنے کی ذمہ داری کفیل لے رہا ہے (۳) مکفول لہ: قرض دینے والا، جس کے لئے کفیل بن رہا ہے (۴) مکفول بہ: وہ مال جس کے ادا کرنے کا کفیل بن رہا ہے، یا وہ آدمی جس کو مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنے کی ذمہ داری لے رہا ہے کہ ابھی اس کو ضمانت پر چھوڑ دیں۔ وقت مقررہ پر اس کو میں مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنے کا ذمہ دار ہوں بشرطیکہ وہ زندہ ہو۔
كفالہ کی دو قسمیں ہیں، كفالہ بالنفس اور كفالہ بالمال۔
كفالہ بالنفس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فلاں آدمی مجلس قضاء میں مقدمہ کے لئے مطلوب ہے اس کو ابھی چھوڑ دیں، میں اس کو وقت مقررہ پر مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنے کا ذمہ دار ہوں۔ اس کو كفالہ بالنفس کہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ ذات اور نفس حاضر کرنے کا کفیل بنا۔
دوسرا ہے كفالہ بالمال: اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فلاں آدمی پر اتنا قرض ہے اس کو ادا کرنے کا میں کفیل اور ذمہ دار ہوں، وہ ادا نہیں کرے گا تو میں اس قرض کو ادا کر دوں گا۔ اس کو كفالہ بالمال کہتے ہیں۔ کیونکہ مال ادا کرنے کی ذمہ داری لے رہا ہے۔
پس كفالہ بالنفس جائز ہے اور اس کی ذمہ داری مکفول بہ کو حاضر کرتا ہے۔
كفالہ بالنفس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مکفول بہ یعنی جس کی ذمہ داری لی ہے اس کو مقررہ وقت میں مجلس قضاء میں حاضر کرنا ہے۔ اس کی دلیل حدیث ہے: سمعت أبا أمامة قال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: العارية مؤداة والمنحة مردودة والدين مقضى والزعيم غارم (أبو داود، الترمذي). اس حدیث میں الزعیم غارم ہے جس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ کفیل ذمہ دار ہے۔ اور اس میں دونوں قسم کے کفیل شامل ہو سکتے ہیں كفیل بالنفس بھی اور كفیل بالمال بھی۔ اس سے كفالہ بالنفس کا ثبوت ہوا۔
اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے حمزہ بن عمرو الاسلمی کو مصدقا بھیجا، فوقع رجل على جارية امرأته فاخذ حمزة من الرجل كفلاء حتى قدم على عمر وكان عمر قد جلده مأة جلدة فصدقهم وعذرهم بالجهالة۔ اور جریر والاشعث لعبد الله بن مسعود في المرتدين استتابهم وكفلهم فتابوا وكفلهم عشائرهم۔ وقال حماد: إذا تكفل بنفس فمات فلا شيء عليه۔ ان دونوں اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ كفالہ بالنفس لینا جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دوسرے کی ذات پر کفیل کا بس نہیں چلے گا اس لئے كفالہ بالنفس لینا جائز نہیں ہے۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ دوسرے کو حاضر کرنے کی استطاعت تو ہے اس لئے كفالہ بالنفس جائز ہے۔
كفالہ بالنفس منعقد ہوتا ہے اگر کہے: میں فلاں کی جان کا كفیل بنا، یا اس کی گردن کا، یا اس کی روح، یا اس کے جسم، یا اس کے سر، یا اس کے آدھے کا، یا اس کی تہائی کا كفیل ہوں۔ قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ ہر وہ لفظ جس سے پورا انسان مراد ہوتا ہو ان الفاظ سے كفالہ بالنفس ہو جائے گا۔ مثلا نفس سے پورا انسان مراد ہوتا ہے۔ اسی طرح گردن بولنے سے پورا انسان مراد لیتے ہیں۔ اسی طرح روح جسم اور سر سے پورا انسان مراد لیتے ہیں۔ اور آدھا اور تہائی کا لفظ پورے انسان میں شائع ہوتے ہیں اس لئے ان لفظوں سے بھی پورا انسان مراد ہوگا اور كفالہ بالنفس ثابت ہو جائے گا۔
Book of Kafalah. Kafalah is of two types: kafalah for the person and kafalah for property. Kafalah for the person is permissible, and what is guaranteed by it is the production of the guaranteed person. It is contracted when he says: 'I guarantee the person of so-and-so' or 'his neck' or 'his soul' or 'his body' or 'his head' or 'half of him' or 'a third of him.' [Urdu commentary: Necessary note: The meaning of kafalah is, for example, Zaid has a debt, so I am responsible for his debt; if he does not pay, I will pay. In the case of kafalah, both people are responsible for paying the debt, and the creditor can collect from either of them. Close to it is hawalah. In that, the original debtor will no longer pay the debt; instead, only I will pay. In that case, the creditor can only collect from the responsible person. The proof for the validity of kafalah is the verse: 'They said: We miss the king's cup, and for whoever brings it is a camel-load, and I am its guarantor.' (Surah Yusuf 72). In this verse is the word za'im, which means responsible and guarantor. The meaning is that whoever brings the king's cup will get a camel-load, and I am its guarantor. This proves kafalah. Regarding Maryam, peace be upon her: 'And Zakariyya guaranteed her' (Surah Al Imran 37). This proves kafalah. There are four terms in kafalah: (1) kafil: he who makes himself responsible, also called dhamin, za'im, and tahammul; (2) makful 'anhu: the debtor on whose behalf the kafil takes responsibility; (3) makful lahu: the creditor for whom the kafil becomes responsible; (4) makful bihi: the property for which he becomes responsible, or the person whom he undertakes to produce in the court, that he be released on bail, and he undertakes to produce him at the appointed time in court, provided he is alive. Kafalah is of two types: kafalah bi al-nafs and kafalah bi al-mal. Kafalah bi al-nafs means that a certain person is required in court for a case; let him go now, and I am responsible for producing him at the appointed time in court. This is called kafalah bi al-nafs because he becomes the guarantor for the person and self. The second is kafalah bi al-mal: meaning that a certain person has a debt of such amount, I am his guarantor and responsible; if he does not pay, I will pay the debt. This is called kafalah bi al-mal because he takes responsibility for paying the property. So kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible and its responsibility is to produce the makful bihi. The meaning of kafalah bi al-nafs is to produce the makful bihi, i.e., the one for whom responsibility is taken, at the appointed time in court. Its proof is the hadith: I heard Abu Umamah say: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: 'The borrowed item is to be returned, the gift is to be given back, the debt is to be paid, and the guarantor is responsible.' (Abu Dawood, Tirmidhi). In this hadith, 'al-za'im gharim' means that the guarantor is responsible. And this includes both types of guarantors: the guarantor for the person and the guarantor for property. Thus kafalah bi al-nafs is proven. There is also evidence in the athar that Umar sent Hamzah ibn 'Amr al-Aslami as a collector, then a man fell upon the slave-girl of his wife, so Hamzah took guarantors for the person from the man until he came to Umar, and Umar had flogged him one hundred lashes; he affirmed them and excused them due to ignorance. And Jarir and al-Ash'ath to 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud regarding the apostates: they made them repent and took sureties for them, so they repented and their tribes gave sureties for them. And Hammad said: If one becomes a guarantor for a person and then the guaranteed person dies, there is nothing upon him. From these two athar, it is known that taking kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible. Imam Shafi'i says that a guarantor has no control over another's person, therefore kafalah bi al-nafs is not permissible. We say that one does have the ability to produce the other, therefore kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible. Kafalah bi al-nafs is contracted if he says: I become a guarantor for the life of so-and-so, or for his neck, or his soul, or his body, or his head, or half of him, or a third of him. The rule is that any word that refers to the entire person constitutes kafalah bi al-nafs. For example, by 'nafs' the entire person is meant. Similarly, by saying 'neck' the entire person is meant. Likewise, by 'soul', 'body', and 'head' the entire person is meant. And the words 'half' and 'third' are spread over the entire person, so by these words also the entire person is intended, and kafalah bi al-nafs is established.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from the book of Kafalah. The author first defines kafalah as having two types: kafalah bil-nafs (suretyship for the person) and kafalah bil-mal (suretyship for property). He then states the ruling that kafalah bil-nafs is permissible (ja'iz), and its content is the production (ihdar) of the guaranteed person (makful bihi) in court. The contracting of kafalah bil-nafs occurs through specific verbal formulas that refer to the whole person: by saying 'I guarantee the person of so-and-so' or 'his neck', 'his soul', 'his body', 'his head', 'half of him', or 'a third of him'. 

The commentary provides the legal proofs. First, the Quranic verse from Surah Yusuf (72) where the word 'za'im' is used, meaning guarantor. This proves the general validity of kafalah. Second, the verse about Maryam 'wa kafalaha Zakariyya' shows kafalah in action. Then the hadith 'al-za'im gharim' (the guarantor is responsible) from Abu Dawood and Tirmidhi directly establishes that a guarantor is liable, which includes both types. Additionally, reports from the Sahaba (athar) show that the Companions practiced kafalah bil-nafs: Hamzah took sureties for a person, and Ibn Mas'ud took sureties for apostates. Hammad's statement that if the guaranteed person dies, the guarantor has no liability shows the limited scope of kafalah bil-nafs. 

The passage also includes a dispute with Imam Shafi'i, who held kafalah bil-nafs invalid because one cannot guarantee another's person (lack of control). The Hanafi response is that one does have istita'ah (ability) to produce the person, as seen in the athar. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that it is permissible. 

The contracting formula is explained by the maxim that any word implying the whole person makes kafalah bil-nafs valid. This includes direct references (nafs, raqaba, ruh, jasad, ra's) and fractional parts (nisf, thulth) because they are considered to encompass the whole person in this context.

Key Terms
كفالة بالنفس (kafalah bi al-nafs): Suretyship for the person.
استطاعة (istita'ah): Ability, capacity; used by Hanafis to argue that the guarantor can produce the person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following expressions is NOT valid for contracting kafalah bil-nafs according to the passage?
A) 'I guarantee his neck' (برقبته)
B) 'I guarantee his soul' (بروحه)
C) 'I guarantee his property' (بماله)
D) 'I guarantee his head' (برأسه)

Key Takeaway
Kafalah bil-nafs is contracted by any word that implies the whole person, and the Hanafi school holds it valid despite the Shafi'i objection, based on the ability to produce the guaranteed person.

Kafalah — Surety

Validity and Wording of Kafalah bi al-Nafs
Ruling on validity and wording of suretyship for person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kafalah bi al-nafs, identify its proof, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Kafalah bi al-nafs is valid because the guarantor can produce the person – 'al-za'eem gharim' proves liability.

This passage establishes that kafalah bi al-nafs (suretyship for the person) is a valid contract in the Hanafi school, supported by the hadith 'al-za'eem gharim' and the practice of the Companions. It also specifies the wording that creates this obligation. This lesson explains the ruling, its evidence, and the key dispute with Imam al-Shafiʿī.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The contract of kafalah bi al-nafs (suretyship for the person). The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) and valid (ja'iz).
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites the hadith 'al-za'eem gharim' from Abu Umamah and athar from Hamzah and Ibn Mas'ud. Identify these as the proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does 'al-za'eem gharim' prove kafalah bi al-nafs? The word 'za'eem' is general, covering both person and property. The hadith establishes that the guarantor is liable, and this liability extends to producing the person.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that kafalah bi al-nafs is invalid because the guarantor has no control over another's person, making it impossible to guarantee.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response is that the guarantor has the ability to produce the person through request or legal means, so the contract is valid.

اور کفالہ با نفس ثابت ہو جائے گا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ فرماتے تھے عاریت پر لی ہوئی چیز ادا کی جائے گی ، عطیہ واپس کیا جائے گا اور دین ادا کیا جانا چاہئے اور کفیل ضامن ہوتا ہے( ب ) حضرت عمر نے حمزہ بن عمر اسلمی کو صدقہ وصول کرنے کے لئے بھیجا۔ پس ایک آدمی نے حضرت عمر کی بیوی کی باندی سے بدکاری کر لی تو حمزہ نے اس آدمی سے کفیل بانفس لئے یہاں تک کہ حضرت عمر آجائے ۔ اور حضرت عمر نے اس کو سو کوڑے لگائے تھے۔ پس اس کی تصدیق کی۔ اور نہ جانے کی وجہ یہ اس کو معذور قرار دیا۔ عبداللہ بن مسعود نے مرتدین سے تو بہ کروائی اور اس سے کفیل لیا، پس ان لوگوں نے توبہ کی اور ان کے خاندان والوں نے کفیل بانفس دیا۔ اور حماد The book of surety is permissible, and what is guaranteed by it is the production of the person guaranteed. (3) And it is concluded when he says: I am surety for the person of so-and-so, or for his neck, or his spirit, or his body, or his head, or half of him, or a third of him. A point: It is not that if he does not undergo the punishment, I will undergo punishment instead. Kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible. Its proof is this hadith: ... then he said: The borrowed item is to be returned, the gift is to be given back, the debt is to be paid, and the guarantor is responsible. In this hadith, 'al-za'eem gharim' means the guarantor is liable. And it includes both types of guarantor: the guarantor of the person and the guarantor of wealth. This proves kafalah bi al-nafs. (2) Its proof is also in the athar that Hamzah took kafalah bi al-nafs for a criminal. ... These two athar show that taking kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible. Benefit: Imam Shafi'i says that the guarantor has no control over the person of another, so kafalah bi al-nafs is not permissible. We say that the ability to produce the person exists, so kafalah bi al-nafs is permissible. (3) Kafalah bi al-nafs is concluded if he says: I am surety for his life, or his neck, or his spirit, or his body, or his head, or half of him, or a third of him. From here, it is mentioned how, or with which words, kafalah bi al-nafs is established. The rule is that any word that implies the whole person establishes kafalah bi al-nafs. For example, 'nafs' means the whole person; similarly, 'neck' implies the whole person; similarly, 'spirit', 'body', and 'head' imply the whole person; and 'half' and 'third' are fractions of the whole person, so they also imply the whole person and kafalah bi al-nafs is established.

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on kafalah (suretyship). The author first states that the chapter is permissible (ja'iz) and that the subject of the guarantee is the production of the person guaranteed (mukful bihi). Then he presents ruling (3): the contract of kafalah bi al-nafs is concluded when the guarantor uses specific words that indicate the whole person, such as 'nafs', 'raqaba', 'ruh', 'jasad', 'ra's', 'nisf', 'thulth'. The Urdu commentary explains that the meaning is not that the guarantor will suffer punishment instead of the original person; rather, it is a guarantee to produce the person. The ruling is supported by the hadith 'al-za'eem gharim' which is general for both person and property, and by athar from the Companions. The author then addresses a dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i, who argued that kafalah bi al-nafs is invalid because the guarantor has no control over the person. The Hanafi response is that the guarantor has the ability to produce the person (by requesting or compelling), so it is valid. The condition for the words is that they denote the entire person; thus, mentioning a part like head or half is acceptable because it refers to the whole. The footnote provides further explanation of the hadith and athar.

Key Terms
كفالة بالنفس (kafalah bi al-nafs): A contract where the guarantor (kafil) undertakes to produce the person of the guaranteed (mukful bihi) before the claimant.
الزعيم غارم (al-za'eem gharim): The guarantor is liable/responsible for the debt or person.
مكفول به (mukful bihi): The person or thing for which guarantee is given; here, the person to be produced.

Key Takeaway
Kafalah bi al-nafs is valid in Hanafi fiqh when the guarantor uses words denoting the whole person, proven by hadith and athar, despite the Shafi'i objection of lack of control.

Kafalah — Surety

Valid Expressions for Kafalah bi al-Nafs
Further valid expressions for surety of person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the valid Arabic expressions that create a contract of kafalah bi al-nafs and explain the evidentiary basis from hadith.

Core Idea
Multiple phrases, including 'على' and 'إلى', establish kafalah if they indicate assumption of responsibility for a person.

In this lesson, we explore the additional phrases that the Hanafi school accepts for creating a surety of person (kafalah bi al-nafs). Beyond the basic formula, words like 'ضمنته', 'هو على', 'إلي', 'زعيم', and 'قبیل' are all valid. The ruling is supported by hadith evidence where the Prophet (PBUH) used similar language to accept liability.

Guided Path
1
List the five additional phrases
The author enumerates specific Arabic expressions that create kafalah: ضمنته, هو على, الي, أنا به زعيم, قبیل به. Each of these phrases indicates assumption of responsibility.
These are synonymous with the basic formula of kafalah.
2
Identify the linguistic link
Each phrase explicitly or implicitly indicates guarantee. The word 'على' is used in a hadith where the Prophet says 'فعلی' (upon me) for debts, showing acceptance of liability.
The word 'على' in classical Arabic is often used for obligations.
3
Examine the hadith evidence
Two hadiths are cited: the hadith of Jabir (Nasa'i) using 'فعلی' and the hadith of Abu Hurairah (Muslim) using 'الینا' (upon us). Both demonstrate that such words create a binding obligation.
The hadiths establish precedent for using these terms in kafalah.
4
Confirm the ruling
Since these phrases are established by prophetic practice, using them in a kafalah contract makes the guarantor liable. The Hanafi position is that any word indicating suretyship is valid.
The ruling is based on the principle that the contract is formed by clear indication of intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وکذالک ان قال ضمنته او هو على او الي او انا به زعيم او قبیل به [۱۴۲۱] (۴) اور ایسے ہی کہا کہ میں اس کا ضامن ہوں یادہ میرے اوپر ہے یا میری طرف ہے یا میں اس کا ذمہ دار ہوں یا میں اس کا کفیل ہوں ان الفاظ کے مہینے سے بھی کفیل ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ الفاظ کفالت پر دلالت کرتے ہیں۔ لفظ علی بھی ذمہ داری قبول کرنے کے لئے آتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔عن جابر قال كان النبي الله لا يصلى على رجل عليه دين ... قال انا اولى بكل مؤمن من نفسه من ترك دین فعلی و من ترك مالا فلورثته (الف) (نسائی شریف، باب الصلوۃ من علیہ دین ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۱۹۶۴) اس حدیث میں فَعَلَی کا لفظ استعمال ہوا ہے جو کفالت کے معنی میں ہے کہ جس نے دین چھوڑا میں اس کا کفیل ہوں۔ اس لئے علی کی وجہ سے بھی کفالت ہو جائے گی۔ والی کا لفظ بھی ذمہ داری اور کفالت کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هــيــرة انه قال من ترك مالا فللورثة ومن ترك كلا فالينا (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب من ترک مالا فلور مختص ۳۵ نمبر ۴۱۶۱/۱۶۱۹) اس حدیث میں الینا نفیل بنے کے معنی میں ہے۔ الزعیم کا لفظ کفیل کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ اس کے لئے قرآن کی آیت اور حدیث الزعیم غارم گزرگئی ہے۔ اور قبیل کے لفظ سے کفالہ ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس سے قبالہ آتا ہے چیک کے معنی میں۔ اور قبالہ بھی کفالت کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے۔
And similarly if he says: I am his guarantor (ضمنته), or he is on me (هو على), or to me (الي), or I am a guarantor (زعيم) for him, or his surety (قبیل). (4) And similarly, if he says: I am his guarantor, or it is upon me, or to me, or I am responsible for him, or I am his surety, with these words he becomes a guarantor. Because these words indicate guarantee. The word 'على' also comes to mean accepting responsibility. In a hadith: ... he said: 'I am more worthy of every believer than himself. Whoever leaves a debt, it is upon me, and whoever leaves wealth, it is for his heirs.' In this hadith, the word 'علی' is used in the sense of guarantee: 'whoever leaves a debt, I am his guarantor.' So guarantee is established by 'على'. The word 'إلى' is also used for responsibility and guarantee. In a hadith: ... he said: 'Whoever leaves wealth, it is for the heirs; and whoever leaves a debt, it is upon us.' In this hadith, 'إلينا' means 'upon us' in the sense of guarantee. The word 'زعيم' is used for guarantor. For it, the Quranic verse and the hadith 'al-za'eem gharim' have already passed. And guarantee is established by the word 'قبیل' because it derives from 'قبالة' meaning a cheque, and 'قبالة' also means guarantee.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage continues the topic of valid phrases for kafalah bi al-nafs. The author lists additional words that establish the contract: 'ضمنته' (I am his guarantor), 'هو على' (he is upon me), 'إلي' (to me), 'زعيم' (responsible), 'قبیل' (surety). The commentary explains that each of these words denotes assumption of responsibility. Evidence is given from hadith: the word 'على' is used by the Prophet (PBUH) to accept liability for debts, so it indicates kafalah. Similarly, 'إلى' in a hadith is used for 'upon us' meaning the Prophet's responsibility. The word 'زعيم' is well-known from the hadith 'al-za'eem gharim'. For 'قبیل', it is derived from 'قبالة' which is a written guarantee, so it also implies suretyship. Thus, these words are effective to create a valid kafalah bi al-nafs contract.

Key Terms
ضمنته (dhamintuhu): I am his guarantor; a phrase that creates kafalah.
هو على (huwa 'alayya): He is upon me, meaning I am responsible for him.
قبیل (qabeel): Surety or guarantor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which hadith word is used as proof that saying 'هو على' creates a valid kafalah?
A) 'فعلی' in the hadith of Jabir
B) 'الینا' in the hadith of Abu Hurairah
C) 'الزعيم غارم'
D) 'العارية مؤداة'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school accepts a wide range of Arabic expressions for kafalah bi al-nafs as long as they indicate assumption of responsibility.

Condition of Time in Kafalah bi al-Nafs and Imprisonment
Consequences of stipulating a time in kafalah bi al-nafs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a guarantor in kafalah bi al-nafs may be imprisoned after failing to produce the guaranteed person at the stipulated time, and identify the proof from the practice of Shurayh.

Core Idea
Stipulating a time makes production binding; failure leads to imprisonment if the person is alive and in Dar al-Islam.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling in kafalah bi al-nafs: when a time is stipulated, the guarantor's obligation becomes binding. If he fails to produce the person despite demand, the judge may imprison him. This ruling is supported by a well-known athar of Qadi Shurayh, who imprisoned his own son for such a breach. We will analyze the conditions that trigger imprisonment and the evidence behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Kafalah bi al-nafs (personal surety) with a stipulation of time. The ruling is that the guarantor must produce the person when demanded at that time; if he fails, the judge may imprison him.
The obligation (wujub) arises from the condition (shart) in the contract.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the practice of Qadi Shurayh, who imprisoned his own son for failing to fulfill a kafalah obligation. This athar is recorded in Musannaf Abd al-Razzaq and other sources.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) from the actions of a prominent early judge.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Shurayh's act of imprisoning his son demonstrates that imprisonment is a legitimate remedy for breach of kafalah bi al-nafs when a time is stipulated. The legal link (wajh) is that failure to produce after a time-bound promise constitutes ghadr (breach of trust), which warrants detention.
The Hanafis consider this practice as evidence for the ruling.
4
Identify the conditions for imprisonment
The passage and commentary specify conditions: (1) a time is stipulated, (2) demand is made at that time, (3) the guarantor fails to produce, (4) the guaranteed person is alive, (5) the person is in Dar al-Islam.
These shurut must all be satisfied for imprisonment to apply.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school permits imprisonment; other schools may not allow this remedy. The difference stems from differing views on the effect of conditions in kafalah.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the broader spectrum of fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان شرط في الكفالة تسليم المكفول به فى وقت بعينه لزمه احضاره اذا طالبه به في ذلك الوقت فان احضره والا حبسه الحاكم. [۱۴۲۲] (۵) پس اگر کفالہ میں شرط کی گئی ہو مشغول بہ کو سپرد کرنے کی مقرر وقت میں تو کفیل کو اس کا حاضر کرنا لازم ہے جب اس کو اس وقت میں مطالبہ کرے، پس اگر اس کو حاضر کر دیا تو ٹھیک ہے ورنہ حاکم کفیل کو قید کر لے گا۔ کفالہ بالنفس میں یہ شرط لگائی تھی کہ مکفول بہ کو تعین وقت میں حاضر کرے گا تو کفیل پر لازم ہے کہ جب مکفول بہ کوطلب کرے اس وقت اس کو حاضر کر دے۔ پس اگر اس نے مقررہ وقت میں مکفول بہ کو حاضر کر دیا تو بہتر ہے۔ اور اگر حاضر نہ کر سکا اور کئی مرتبہ مطالبہ کے بعد بھی حاضر نہیں کیا اور ملکول بہ زندہ ہے اور دار الاسلام میں موجود ہے تو اب کفیل کو حاکم قید کرے گا۔ اس نے وعدہ خلافی کی اور دوسرے کا حق مارا اس لئے اس کو قید کرے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت موجود ہے کہ حج اف وعدہ پر حضرت شریح نے خود اپنے بیٹے کو قید کیا ۔ سمعت حبيبا الذي كان يقدم الخصوم الى شريح قال خاصم رجل ابنا لشريح الى شريح كفل له برجل علیه دین فحبسه شریح فلما كان الليل قال اذهب الى عبد الله بفراش وطعام وكان ابنه يسمى عبد الله (ج) ( سنن سیھتی ، باب ما جاء في الكفالته بدن من علیه حق، ج سادس ، ص ۱۲۸، نمبر ۱۳۱۸ در مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الكفلاء ، ج ثامن، ، ماجاء ۱۱۴۱۸ر حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا میں ہر مؤمن کے نفس سے بھی زیادہ قریب ہوں۔ جس نے قرض چھوڑ اوہ مجھ پر ہے۔ اور جس نے مال چھوڑ اوہ اس کے ورثہ کے لئے ہے (ب) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے مال چھوڑ اوہ اس کے ورثہ کے لئے ہے۔ اور قرض چھوڑا وہ ہمارے ذمہ ہے (ج) حضرت حبیب فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک آدمی نے شریح کے پاس اس کے بیٹے کو جھگڑے کے لئے لے گیا جو ایک آدمی پر قرض کا کفیل بنا تھا۔ تو قاضی شریح نے اس کو قید کر لیا۔ پس رات ہوئی تو ( باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
If delivery of the guaranteed person is stipulated at a specific time, it becomes obligatory for the guarantor to produce him when demanded at that time. If he produces him, fine; otherwise, the judge will imprison him. (5) So if in the kafalah, a condition was made to hand over the person at a specified time, then the guarantor is obliged to produce him when demanded at that time. If he produces him at the appointed time, it is good; otherwise, if he cannot produce him and after repeated demands still does not produce him, and the guaranteed person is alive and present in the abode of Islam, then the judge will imprison the guarantor. Because he has broken his promise and violated the right of another. There is evidence in the athar that on a similar commitment, Shurayh himself imprisoned his own son. ... (hadith of Shurayh) Footnote: (a) The Prophet said: I am closer to every believer than his own self; whoever leaves a debt, it is upon me; whoever leaves wealth, it is for his heirs. (b) The Prophet said: Whoever leaves wealth, it is for his heirs; whoever leaves a debt, it is upon us. (c) Habib narrated that a man brought Shurayh's son to him for a dispute, as he had stood surety for a man's debt, so Shurayh imprisoned him. Then at night, he said to go to Abdullah with bedding and food - and his son was named Abdullah. (The rest is on the next page.)
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific condition in kafalah bi al-nafs: if the contract stipulates a deadline for producing the guaranteed person, the guarantor is obligated to produce him when demanded within that time. If he fails to do so, the judge (hakim) has the authority to imprison the guarantor. The commentary explains that this is because the guarantor has broken his promise and violated the right of the claimant. The ruling is supported by an athar of Qadi Shurayh, who imprisoned his own son for failing to fulfill a kafalah obligation. This indicates that imprisonment is a legitimate remedy in Hanafi fiqh for such breach. The footnotes provide additional context from hadith about the Prophet's responsibility for debts.

Key Terms
شرط (shart): A condition in the contract specifying a time for delivery of the person.
حبس (habs): Imprisonment by the judge as a consequence for breaching the kafalah obligation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does the Hanafi school allow the judge to imprison the guarantor in kafalah bi al-nafs?
A) If the guarantor fails to produce the person on the stipulated time
B) If the guaranteed person has died
C) If the guarantor is poor
D) If the claimant demands money instead

Key Takeaway
Stipulating a time in kafalah bi al-nafs creates a binding obligation; failure leads to imprisonment only if the person is alive and in Dar al-Islam.

Kafalah — Surety
beginner
6 min
Valid Expressions for Kafalah: ضممتہ‎, علی‎, الی‎, زعیم‎, قبیل
Lists and proves valid expressions for kafalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six valid Arabic expressions that establish kafalah in the Hanafi school and cite the hadith proofs for each.

Core Idea
Kafalah is valid with any clear indication of assuming responsibility, not only specific formulaic words.

In the Hanafi school, the validity of a kafalah (suretyship) contract depends on clear expression of assuming responsibility. This lesson enumerates the specific Arabic terms that are recognized by the school as establishing a valid kafalah, each supported by textual evidence from the Qur'an or Sunnah. Understanding these expressions is essential for correctly forming a kafalah contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed expressions
Read the Arabic text and list the six words/phrases cited: ضمنته‎, هو علىّ‎, إلىّ‎, أنا به زعيم‎, قبیل‎, and implicitly كفلته from the context. Each is a valid lafz for kafalah.
The Urdu commentary adds كفيل as equivalent to زعيم.
2
Analyze the proof for each expression
For each expression, locate the specific dalil provided: for 'على' the hadith of Jabir (Nasa'i) using 'فعلى'; for 'إلى' the hadith of Abu Hurayrah (Muslim) using 'إلينا'; for 'زعيم' the verse and hadith 'الزعيم غارم'; for 'قبیل' the derivation from 'قبالة' meaning check/guarantee. Note that 'ضمنته' and 'كفلته' are directly understood.
The proofs are ahadith zanni al-thubut but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Understand the Hanafi principle of lafz in contracts
The Hanafi school accepts any wording that clearly indicates the assumption of liability, unlike some schools that require specific formulaic words. This is based on the principle of 'al-ibrah bi al-ma'ani la bi al-alfaz' (consideration is given to meanings, not words).
This principle explains why multiple expressions are valid.
4
Apply the ruling to a sample scenario
Given a situation where someone says 'I am responsible for his debt' without using a specific term, determine if kafalah is established. Using the Hanafi criterion, since the meaning is clear, the kafalah is valid.
Practice distinguishing between explicit and ambiguous expressions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و کذالک ان قال ضمنته اوهو على او الي او انا به زعيم او قبیل به
اور ایسے ہی کہا کہ میں اس کا ضامن ہوں یادہ میرے اوپر ہے یا میری طرف ہے یا میں اس کا ذمہ دار ہوں یا میں اس کا کفیل ہوں ان الفاظ کے مہینے سے بھی کفیل ہو جائے گا۔
کیونکہ یہ الفاظ کفالت پر دلالت کرتے ہیں۔ لفظ علی بھی ذمہ داری قبول کرنے کے لئے آتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔عن جابر قال كان النبي الله لا يصلى على رجل عليه دين ... قال انا اولى بكل مؤمن من نفسه من ترک دین فعلی و من ترک مالا فلورثته (الف) (نسائی شریف، باب الصلوۃ من علیہ دین ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۱۹۶۴) اس حدیث میں فَعَلَی کا لفظ استعمال ہوا ہے جو کفالت کے معنی میں ہے کہ جس نے دین چھوڑا میں اس کا کفیل ہوں۔ اس لئے علی کی وجہ سے بھی کفالت ہو جائے گی۔ اور الٹی کا لفظ بھی ذمہ داری اور کفالت کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابي هــيــرة انه قال من ترك مالا فللورثة ومن ترك كلا فالينا (ب) (مسلم شریف، باب من ترک مالا فلور مختص ۳۵ نمبر ۴۱۶۱/۱۶۱۹) اس حدیث میں الینا نفیل بنے کے معنی میں ہے۔ الزعیم کا لفظ کفیل کے لئے استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ اس کے لئے قرآن کی آیت اور حدیث الزعیم غارم گزرگئی ہے۔ اور قبیل کے لفظ سے کفالہ ہوگا اس کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس سے قبالہ آتا ہے چیک کے معنی میں۔ اور قبالہ بھی کفالت کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے۔
And similarly if he said: I am his guarantor, or it is upon me, or to me, or I am his surety (za'im), or he is under my responsibility (qabil). And likewise if he said: I am his guarantor, it is on me, or towards me, or I am the guarantor (dhimmah dar), or I am his surety (kafil) — by these words too he becomes a kafil. Because these words indicate kafalah. The word 'ala' is used for accepting responsibility. There is a hadith: from Jabir that the Prophet (peace be upon him) would not pray over a man who had a debt... he said: I am closer to every believer than his own self; whoever leaves a debt, it is upon me; whoever leaves wealth, it is for his heirs. (Nasa'i) In this hadith the word 'fa'ala' is used meaning kafalah: whoever leaves a debt, I am his kafil. Therefore kafalah is established by 'ala'. And the word 'ila' is also used for responsibility and kafalah. There is a hadith: from Abu Hurairah that he said: whoever leaves wealth, it is for his heirs; whoever leaves debt, it is upon us. (Muslim) In this hadith 'ilayna' means kafalah. The word 'za'im' is used for kafil. Its evidence from the Qur'an and hadith 'al-za'im gharim' has passed. And kafalah is established by the word 'qabil'; its evidence is that from it comes 'qabalah' meaning a check, and 'qabalah' is also used in the meaning of kafalah.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage enumerates and proves the valid expressions (al-alfaz) by which kafalah (suretyship) is established in the Hanafi school. The author lists six words: damintuhu (I am his guarantor), huwa 'alayya (it is upon me), ilayya (to me), ana bihi za'im (I am his surety), qabil (under my responsibility), and also includes kafaltuhu (from the broader context). Each word is supported by textual evidence: 'ala' is proven by the hadith of Jabir where the Prophet used 'fa'ala' for debt; 'ila' is proven by the hadith of Abu Hurairah using 'ilayna'; 'za'im' is a known term for guarantor with its own verse and hadith; 'qabil' is linked to 'qabalah' which means guarantee. The commentary explains that these words all indicate an assumption of responsibility, thus validly creating a kafalah contract.

Key Terms
ضمنته (damintuhu): I am his guarantor; a direct statement of guarantee.
على ('ala): Upon me/on my responsibility; indicates assumption of liability.
الى (ila): To me/towards me; indicates responsibility.
زعيم (za'im): Surety/guarantor; one who takes responsibility for another.
قبیل (qabil): Under my responsibility; from the root q-b-l meaning to accept or undertake.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following words is proven by the hadith in Sunan al-Nasa'i to establish kafalah?
A) ضمنته
B) على
C) زعيم
D) قبیل

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates kafalah using any clear expression of assuming responsibility, such as ضمنته‎, على‎, إلى‎, زعيم‎, and قبیل, supported by hadith evidence.

Conditional Delivery in Kafalah and Imprisonment for Default
Ruling on conditional delivery in kafalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a delivery time is stipulated in kafalah and explain the judge's authority to imprison the kafil upon default.

Core Idea
If a kafil fails to produce the person at the agreed time, the judge may imprison him.

The kafalah contract can include a condition for the surety to produce the guaranteed person at a specific time. This lesson examines the ruling when such a condition is made and the consequence of failure: imprisonment of the kafil. The ruling is supported by the practice of the Companion Qadi Shuraih.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contract and condition
The kafalah contract has a shart (condition) requiring delivery of the makful bihi at a specified time. This condition creates an additional obligation.
2
Determine the obligation (wajib)
The kafil must bring the person when demanded at that time. This is wajib (obligatory) due to the condition.
The obligation is on the kafil, not on the makful bihi.
3
Identify the consequence of failure
If the kafil fails to produce the person after demand, the judge (hakim) has the authority to imprison the kafil. This is a punitive measure for breach of promise.
Imprisonment is for the kafil's default, not for the debt itself.
4
Examine the dalil
The ruling is supported by the practice of Qadi Shuraih, a Companion of the Prophet, who imprisoned his own son for failing to produce a debtor he had guaranteed.
The hadith is: 'From Habib: A man brought a son of Shuraih before Shuraih concerning a debt guarantee, so Shuraih imprisoned him.'
5
Understand the limits
Imprisonment applies only if the makful bihi is alive and within Dar al-Islam (the land of Islam). If the person is dead or outside the realm, the ruling may differ.
The passage specifies these conditions in the Urdu commentary.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان شرط في الكفالة تسليم المكفول به فى وقت بعينه لزمه احضاره اذا طالبه به في ذلك الوقت فان احضره والا حبسه الحاكم.
پس اگر کفالہ میں شرط کی گئی ہو مشغول بہ کو سپرد کرنے کی مقرر وقت میں تو کفیل کو اس کا حاضر کرنا لازم ہے جب اس کو اس وقت میں مطالبہ کرے، پس اگر اس کو حاضر کر دیا تو ٹھیک ہے ورنہ حاکم کفیل کو قید کر لے گا۔
کفالہ بالنفس میں یہ شرط لگائی تھی کہ مکفول بہ کو تعین وقت میں حاضر کرے گا تو کفیل پر لازم ہے کہ جب مکفول بہ کوطلب کرے اس وقت اس کو حاضر کر دے۔ پس اگر اس نے مقررہ وقت میں مکفول بہ کو حاضر کر دیا تو بہتر ہے۔ اور اگر حاضر نہ کر سکا اور کئی مرتبہ مطالبہ کے بعد بھی حاضر نہیں کیا اور ملکول بہ زندہ ہے اور دار الاسلام میں موجود ہے تو اب کفیل کو حاکم قید کرے گا۔
اس نے وعدہ خلافی کی اور دوسرے کا حق مارا اس لئے اس کو قید کرے گا (۲) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت موجود ہے کہ حج اف وعدہ پر حضرت شریح نے خود اپنے بیٹے کو قید کیا ۔ سمعت حبيبا الذي كان يقدم الخصوم الى شريح قال خاصم رجل ابنا لشريح الى شريح
كفل له برجل علیه دین فحبسه شریح فلما كان الليل قال اذهب الى عبد الله بفراش وطعام وكان ابنه يسمى عبد الله (ج) ( سنن سیھتی ، باب ما جاء في الكفالته بدن من علیه حق، ج سادس ، ص ۱۲۸، نمبر ۱۳۱۸ در مصنف عبدالرزاق ، باب الكفلاء ، ج ثامن، ، ماجاء ۱۱۴۱۸ر
حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا میں ہر مؤمن کے نفس سے بھی زیادہ قریب ہوں۔ جس نے قرض چھوڑ اوہ مجھ پر ہے۔ اور جس نے مال چھوڑ اوہ اس کے ورثہ کے لئے ہے
(ب) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے مال چھوڑ اوہ اس کے ورثہ کے لئے ہے۔ اور قرض چھوڑا وہ ہمارے ذمہ ہے
(ج) حضرت حبیب فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک آدمی نے شریح کے پاس اس کے بیٹے کو جھگڑے کے لئے لے گیا جو ایک آدمی پر قرض کا کفیل بنا تھا۔ تو قاضی شریح نے اس کو قید کر لیا۔ پس رات ہوئی تو ( باقی اگلے صفحہ پر )
(صفحہ ۳۰۷ پر) کہا عبداللہ کے پاس جاؤ کھانے اور بستر کے لئے ۔ عبد اللہ قاضی شریح کے دوسرے بیٹے کا نام ہے
If he stipulated in the kafalah the delivery of the person at a specific time, it becomes obligatory for him to bring him when he is demanded at that time. If he brings him, [well and good]; otherwise the judge will imprison him. (Urdu explanation) ... The judge imprisoned him due to breach of promise.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage states a ruling about a conditional kafalah where a specific time for producing the person is agreed. The kafil (surety) is obligated to bring the makful bihi (the person guaranteed) at that time. If he fails, the judge may imprison him. The author supports this with the practice of Qadi Shuraih, who imprisoned his own son for failing to produce a debtor he had guaranteed. This shows that imprisonment is a legitimate consequence for breach of the kafalah promise. The ruling applies when the person is alive and within Dar al-Islam.

Key Terms
كفالة (kafalah): A contract of guarantee or surety, where one person (kafil) guarantees the presence or debt of another (makful bihi/makful 'anhu).
حبس (habs): Imprisonment by the judge as a penalty for failing to fulfill kafalah.
شرط (shart): A condition stipulated in the contract, which here specifies a fixed time for delivery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition may the judge imprison the kafil?
A) If the kafil refuses to pay the debt
B) If the kafil fails to produce the makful bihi at the agreed time
C) If the makful bihi dies
D) If the kafil denies being a surety

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits the judge to imprison a kafil who defaults on a conditional delivery, based on the precedent of Qadi Shuraih.

Discharge of Surety: The Condition of Deliverable Location for Litigation
Condition for discharge of surety by delivery

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for the discharge of a kafil and explain why the place of delivery matters.

Core Idea
A surety is discharged only if he delivers the debtor in a place where the creditor can sue — mere delivery anywhere is insufficient.

This lesson examines the key condition for a kafil (surety) to be freed from his obligation of producing the debtor. The ruling highlights that the purpose of kafalah bi al-nafs is to enable the creditor to pursue his claim legally. Thus, the place of delivery must allow the creditor to initiate legal proceedings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the act is the delivery of the debtor by the surety, and the ruling is that the surety is discharged (bari) from the kafalah.
2
Identify the condition for discharge
Locate the condition explicitly in the text: delivery must be 'in a place where the creditor can sue him' (muhakamah).
The Arabic phrase is 'في مكان يقدر المكفول له على محاكمته'.
3
Understand the rationale (hikmah)
The purpose (maqsad) of kafalah bi al-nafs is to ensure the creditor's access to the debtor for legal claims. If the place does not permit legal action, the purpose is defeated.
This rationale is derived from the commentary and the word 'muhakamah'.
4
Apply the condition
When evaluating a scenario of delivery, ask: 'Can the creditor legally sue the debtor in that location?' If yes, discharge occurs; if no, the surety remains liable.
Consider jurisdiction, type of court, and the creditor's legal standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا احضره وسلمه في مكان يقدر المكفول له على محاكمته برئ الكفيل من ال الكفالة
اگر مکفول بہ کو حضر کر دیا اور سپرد کر دیا ایسی جگہ کہ مکفول لہ اس سے جھگڑا کر سکتا ہے تو کفیل کفالت سے بری ہو جائے گا۔
کفالت کا مقصد ہے کہ ایسی جگہ مکفول بہ کو حاضر کر دے جس سے مکفول لہ اس سے جھگڑا کر سکے، اور کفیل نے ایسا ہی کیا کہ ایسی جگہ حاضر کر دیا جہاں مکفول لہ جھگڑا کر سکتا ہے اس لئے کفیل بری ہو جائے گا۔
And when he brings him and delivers him in a place where the creditor can sue him (take him to court), the surety is discharged from the kafalah.
If the person is brought and handed over in such a place that the creditor can sue him, then the surety is discharged from the kafalah.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage states the condition for the kafil's discharge: he must deliver the person in a place where the creditor can legally initiate a lawsuit against him. The purpose of kafalah bi al-nafs is to ensure the creditor's access to the debtor for claims. Therefore, delivering the person in a place where the creditor cannot effectively sue does not fulfill the purpose, and the kafil remains liable.

Key Terms
محاکمہ (muhakamah): Legal proceeding or lawsuit; the ability to take the person to court.

Key Takeaway
A surety is discharged only when he delivers the debtor in a place that permits the creditor to sue; otherwise, he remains liable.

Death of the Principal Discharges the Surety
Ruling on death of makful bihi ending kafalah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the death of the makful bihi in kafalah bi al-nafs and explain the legal reasoning (illah) for discharge.

Core Idea
The accessory obligation ends when the principal obligation becomes impossible due to death.

This passage addresses a key scenario in kafalah: if a person guarantees to produce someone (kafalah bi al-nafs) and that person dies, what is the surety's obligation? The text rules that the kafil is discharged completely. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof from early authorities, and the reasoning based on impossibility and the accessory nature of the guarantee.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is kafalah bi al-nafs (personal surety). The ruling is that the kafalah becomes void upon the death of the makful bihi—the kafil is discharged.
This is an automatic cancellation, not a penalty.
2
Locate the dalil
The text cites an athar from al-Hakam and Hammad (early authorities) who differed on whether the kafil becomes liable for dirhams. The text adopts the view that nothing is due.
The athar is from Sunan al-Bayhaqi, hadith 11419.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The chosen opinion in the athar directly supports the ruling of discharge. The opposing opinion is not followed because the object of the guarantee (the person) no longer exists.
The proof is not Quran or Sunnah but a qawl sahabi.
4
Analyze the Hanafi reasoning
The kafil is an accessory (tabi'); when the principal's obligation (producing the person) becomes impossible, the accessory also ends. Also, the purpose of kafalah bi al-nafs is to ensure presence; death makes that impossible.
No financial obligation is transferred automatically.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
Some early authorities (e.g., al-Hakam according to one narration) said the kafil must pay dirhams. The Hanafi school rejects this because it treats personal surety like financial guarantee.
This ikhtilaf shows the importance of correctly identifying the nature of the guarantee.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا مات المكفول به برئ الكفيل ص ۱۷۳ نمبر ۱۴۷۶۶)
اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کفیل کے وعدہ خلافی پر اس کو قید کیا جاسکتا ہے۔
اگر مکفول به مرجائے تو کفیل بالنفس کفالہ سے بری ہو جائے گا۔
کفیل نے مجرم کو حاضر کرنے کی کفالت لی تھی لیکن خود مجرم کا انتقال ہو گیا تو کفیل سے کفالہ ساقط ہو جائے گا۔
(۱) مرجانے کی وجہ سے اب حاضر کس کو کرے گا؟ اور مکفول بہ کا مال تو اس کام کے لئے نہیں ہے اس لئے کفالہ ساقط ہو جائے گا (۲) مرنے کی وجہ سے اصیل یعنی مکفول بہ پر حاضر ہونا ساقط ہو گیا اس لئے تابع یعنی کفیل پر بھی ساقط ہو جائے گا (۳) اثر میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن الحكم و حماد انهما قالا في رجل تكفل بنفس رجل فمات الرجل قال احدهما يضمن الدراهم وقال الآخر ليس عليه شيء (الف) (سن سبیھقی ، باب ماجاء فی الكفالة بدن من علی حق ، ج سادس ص ۱۲۸، نمبر ۱۱۴۱۹) اس میں ہے کہ عليه حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حکم اور حماد نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی کسی آدمی کا کفیل بالنفس بنا پھر وہ آدمی مر گیا۔ ان میں سے ایک نے کہا درہم کا ضامن ہوگا اور دوسرے نے فرمایا کھیل پر کچھ نہیں ہے۔
And when the person dies, the surety is discharged. (page 173, no. 14766)
If the guaranteed person dies, the kafil bi al-nafs is discharged from the kafalah. ... Evidence: from al-Hakam and Hammad: they said concerning a man who became surety for a man and then the man died, one of them said he is liable for the dirhams, and the other said nothing is upon him.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage rules that the death of the makful bihi (the person guaranteed) automatically discharges the kafil. The reasoning is threefold: (1) the object of the kafalah (producing the person) becomes impossible; (2) since the principal (the person) is no longer required to appear, the accessory (the surety) is also discharged; (3) there is an athar (report from early authorities) that al-Hakam and Hammad differed on whether the kafil becomes liable for money instead, but the majority view (and the text's stance) is that nothing is due. The commentary prefers the view that kafalah is entirely cancelled.

Key Terms
اصیل (asil): The principal person (makful bihi) who is the subject of the guarantee.
تابع (tabi'): The accessory (kafil) whose obligation follows the principal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The kafil becomes liable to pay the debt
B) The kafil is discharged from the kafalah
C) The kafalah continues and the kafil must produce the body
D) The kafil must find a substitute

Key Takeaway
In kafalah bi al-nafs, the kafil is discharged when the makful bihi dies because the object of the guarantee (the person) no longer exists.

Discharge of Guarantor by Delivery in a Litigable Place
Ruling on discharge of kafeel in kafalah bil nafs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition under which a kafeel is freed from kafalah bil nafs and explain the rationale behind the place requirement.

Core Idea
Delivering the principal to a place where the creditor can sue frees the guarantor.

In kafalah bil nafs, the guarantor undertakes to produce the principal when required. This lesson addresses the key condition for the guarantor's discharge: the place of delivery must enable the creditor to initiate litigation. Understanding this condition clarifies the purpose of kafalah bil nafs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the Arabic sentence: if the kafeel brings the principal and hands him over in a place where the creditor can litigate, the kafeel is freed from the guarantee.
The ruling is a legal consequence (hukm wad'i) of fulfilling a condition.
2
Isolate the condition
The key phrase is 'fi makan yaqdir al-makful lahu 'ala muhakamatihi' — 'in a place where the creditor can litigate against him'. This is the operative condition.
The condition is not just any delivery; it must be in a place with accessible legal process.
3
Understand the rationale
The Urdu commentary explains: 'The purpose of kafalah is to produce the principal where the creditor can dispute.' Thus, the place requirement aligns with the maqsad (objective) of the guarantee.
If the place does not allow litigation, the guarantee's purpose is not fulfilled.
4
Apply the condition
If the principal is delivered in a place where the creditor cannot sue (e.g., a remote area without courts), the kafeel is not discharged. The text implies this by negative inference.
The kafeel must ensure the creditor has practical access to claim his right.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1423 (6)] واذا احضره وسلمه في مكان يقدر المكفول له على محاكمته برئ الكفيل من ال الكفالة اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ کفیل کے وعدہ خلافی پر اس کو قید کیا جاسکتا ہے۔ (۱۳۲۳) (۲) اگر مکفول بہ کو حضر کر دیا اور سپرد کر دیا ایسی جگہ کہ مکفول لہ اس سے جھگڑا کر سکتا ہے تو کفیل کفالت سے بری ہو جائے گا۔ کفالت کا مقصد ہے کہ ایسی جگہ مکفول بہ کو حاضر کر دے جس سے مکفول لہ اس سے جھگڑا کر سکے، اور کفیل نے ایسا ہی کیا کہ ایسی جگہ حاضر کر دیا جہاں مکفول لہ جھگڑا کر سکتا ہے اس لئے کفیل بری ہو جائے گا۔
And if he brings him (the principal) and hands him over in a place where the person for whom he is surety (the creditor) can litigate against him, the guarantor is freed from the guarantee. From this it is understood that the guarantor can be imprisoned for breaking his promise. (1323) (2) If the principal is produced and handed over in a place where the creditor can dispute with him, then the guarantor becomes free from the guarantee. The purpose of the guarantee is to produce the principal in a place where the creditor can dispute with him, and the guarantor has done so by producing him in a place where the creditor can dispute, so the guarantor becomes free.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage states a ruling (hukm) regarding kafalah bil nafs: if the guarantor produces the principal in a place where the creditor has the ability to bring him to court (i.e., where legal proceedings are possible), the guarantor is discharged from his obligation. The Urdu commentary explains that if the guarantor initially promised to produce the debtor but failed, he may be imprisoned. However, once he actually delivers the debtor to a location where the creditor can litigate, the guarantee ends. The key condition is the creditor's ability to access legal process against the debtor. This ruling is from the matn of Al-Quduri or similar, and the commentary expands on the rationale: the guarantee's purpose is to enable the creditor to obtain his right through judicial means.

Key Terms
كفالة بالنفس (kafalah bil nafs): A contract where the guarantor (kafeel) undertakes to produce the principal (makful bih) when required.
مكفول له (makful lahu): The creditor or person to whom the guarantee is given; he has a right against the principal.
محاكمته (muhakamatuhu): The ability to bring the principal to court for litigation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) When he delivers the principal to a place where the creditor can litigate against him.
C) When the principal is taken into custody by the state.
D) When the guarantor pays the debt himself.

Key Takeaway
In kafalah bil nafs, the kafeel is discharged only when the principal is produced in a place enabling the creditor to initiate legal proceedings.
