Guarantor's Right to Recover Payment with Permission
Ruling with proof on guarantor's recourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for the guarantor's right to recover payment and apply the distinction between permission and non-permission.

Core Idea
A guarantor recovers from the principal only if he paid with the principal's permission.

In Hanafi fiqh, the guarantor (kafil) who pays a debt on behalf of the principal (makful anhu) may or may not have the right to recover that payment. The key factor is whether he acted with the principal's permission. This lesson examines the ruling, its evidence from the Sunnah, and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on guarantor's recovery
Identify the exact ruling: the guarantor recovers from the principal if he paid with permission.
This is the core legal rule.
2
Identify the proofs cited (dalil naqli)
Locate the two hadiths used as evidence: (1) the Prophet became guarantor and paid the debt, (2) the hadith of the three dirhams.
Both are ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each hadith proves the ruling. The first hadith shows the Prophet paying without taking the debtor's gold, implying the guarantor's right. The second hadith explicitly shows recovery after payment with permission.
The Prophet's action establishes the principle.
4
Distinguish the condition of permission
Contrast the scenario with payment without permission, where the payment is considered a gift and no recovery is allowed.
Permission is the decisive factor.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Recognize that Shafi'is also allow recovery but may differ on conditions; the Hanafi position requires explicit permission.
A valid ikhtilaf exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1435] (18) فان كفل بامره رجع بما يؤدى عليه. پس اگر کفیل بنا مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے تو لے لے گا وہ جو کچھ اس پر ادا کرے۔ مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے کفیل بنا تھا تو کفیل نے جتنی رقم مکفول لہ کو دی ہے اتنی رقم مکفول عنہ سے وصول کرے گا۔ (۱) مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے کفیل نے اپنا روپیہ مکفول لہ کو دیا ہے اس لئے وہ مکفول عنہ سے وصول کرنے کا حق رکھتا ہے (۲) عن ابن عباس ان رجلا لزم غريما له بعشرة دنانير فقال والله ما افارقك حتى تقضينی او تأتيني بحميل قال فتحمل بها النبي الله فـاتـاه بقدر ما وعده فقال له النبى الله الله من اين اصبت هذا الذهب ؟ قال من معدن قال لا حاجة لنا فيها ليس فيها خير فقضاها عنه رسول الله الله (ب) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی استخراج المعادن ص ۱۶ نمبر ۳۳۲۸ را بن ماجه شریف) حاشیہ : (الف) آپ جنازے پر آئے کہ اس پر نماز پڑھے حضرت ابو قتادہ نے فرمایا مجھ پر اس کا دین ہے یا رسول اللہ ! پس آپ نے اس پر نماز پڑھی (ب) ایک آدمی کا قرض خواہ دس دینار کی وجہ سے اس کے پیچھے لگا۔ کہنے لگا خدا کی قسم تم کو نہیں چھوڑوں گا یہاں تک کہ تم قرض ادا کر دو یا کوئی کفیل لاؤ۔ پس حضور اس کے کفیل بنے۔ پس اس آدمی نے وعدہ کے مقدار حضور کے پاس رقم لایا، پس حضور نے پوچھا یہ سونا کہاں سے لائے؟ کہا کان سے۔ آپ نے فرمایا اس کی ضرورت نہیں جس چیز میں خیر نہ ہو۔ پھر حضور نے اپنی جانب سے قرض ادا کیا (ب) ابن عباس نے فرمایا آپ نے فرمایا جس کا میں نے مال لیا تو یہ مال حاضر ہے، اس سے لے لے، پس ایک آدمی کھڑا ہوا اور کہا اے اللہ کے رسول ! میرے آپ کے ذمے تین درہم ہیں۔ آپ نے فرمایا میرا طریقہ یہ ہے کہ میں کہنے والے کو جھلاتا نہیں اور قسم نہیں لیتا کس چیز کی رقم میرے ذمہ ہے۔ اس آدمی نے کہا آپ کو یاد نہیں کہ آپ کے سامنے سے ایک سائل گزرا تو آپ نے مجھے حکم دیا کہ میں اس کو تین درہم دے دوں ۔ آپ نے فرمایا اے فضل ! اس کو تین درہم دیدو (ب) (سنن بیہقی، باب رجوع الضامن على المضمون عنه بما غرم و من با مره، ج سادس صص ۱۲۳ نمبر ۱۱۴۰۳ ) اس حدیث میں حضور کے حکم سے ایک آدمی نے تین درہم دیا تھا اور کفیل بنا تھا اس لئے انہوں نے حضور سے واپس لیا ، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مکفول عنہ کے حکم سے کفیل بنا ہو تو مکفول عنہ سے وصول کرسکتا ہے۔
[1435] (18) So if he becomes surety with his permission, he recovers what he pays. So if the guarantor was made with the permission of the principal, he will take whatever he pays. If he was made guarantor with the principal's permission, then the amount the guarantor gave to the creditor (makful lahu), that amount he will collect from the principal. (1) Because with the principal's permission, the guarantor gave his own money to the creditor, so he has the right to collect from the principal. (2) From Ibn Abbas: A man pressed his debtor for ten dinars, saying, 'By Allah, I will not leave you until you pay me or bring a guarantor.' Then the Prophet (peace be upon him) became guarantor for him. Then the man brought the amount promised to the Prophet, and the Prophet asked, 'Where did you get this gold?' He said, 'From a mine.' He said, 'We have no need of it; there is no good in it.' Then the Messenger of Allah paid the debt for him. (Abu Dawood, chapter on extracting minerals, no. 3328; Ibn Majah) Footnote: (a) He came to the funeral to pray over it; Abu Qatada said, 'His debt is upon me, O Messenger of Allah,' so he prayed over him. (b) A creditor followed his debtor for ten dinars. He said, 'By Allah, I will not leave you until you pay or bring a guarantor.' So the Prophet became his guarantor. Then the man brought the amount promised to the Prophet, and the Prophet asked, 'Where did you get this gold?' He said, 'From a mine.' He said, 'We have no need of it; there is no good in it.' Then the Messenger of Allah paid the debt himself. (b) Ibn Abbas said: The Prophet said, 'Whoever I have taken property from, this property is present; let him take from it.' Then a man stood up and said, 'O Messenger of Allah, I have three dirhams due to me from you.' The Prophet said, 'I do not deny a speaker, and I do not take an oath; what is due to me?' The man said, 'Do you not remember that a beggar passed by you, and you ordered me to give him three dirhams?' He said, 'O Fadl, give him three dirhams.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the guarantor's recourse against the principal for what he paid when with permission, vol. 6, p. 123, no. 11403) In this hadith, a man gave three dirhams by the Prophet's order and became guarantor, so he recovered from the Prophet, showing that if one becomes guarantor with the principal's permission, he can recover from the principal.
Source pages p. 312

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that if the guarantor (kafil) became surety with the permission of the principal (makful anhu), then he is entitled to recover from the principal whatever he paid to the creditor. The reasoning is that the guarantor is spending his own money at the principal's behest, essentially as an agent, so he has the right to reimbursement. Two hadith proofs are cited: (1) The story of the Prophet becoming guarantor for a debtor and later paying the debt; although the debtor brought gold from a mine, the Prophet refused it and paid himself, implying the guarantor's right to recover from the principal. (2) The hadith where a man paid three dirhams by the Prophet's order and later recovered them from the Prophet. The Prophet explicitly allowed the recovery, establishing the principle that the guarantor can seek repayment from the principal when he acted with permission.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-ruju'): The guarantor's right to claim reimbursement from the principal after paying the debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only if the principal was present at the time of payment
B) Only if the guarantor became surety with the principal's permission
C) Always, regardless of permission
D) Only if the debt was for food or necessity

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi kafalah, the guarantor's right to recovery hinges on the principal's permission—without it, the payment is deemed a gift.

Guarantor's Recovery: Payment Without Permission
States rule and proves with hadith of Abu Qatada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that a guarantor who pays without the principal's command has no right of recourse, and apply the hadith proof to identify when payment is considered a voluntary donation.

Core Idea
A guarantor who pays without the principal's command cannot recover; the payment is a voluntary donation (tabarru').

This lesson examines a key ruling in Hanafi law of suretyship (kafalah): if someone guarantees a debt and pays it without being asked by the principal debtor, does he have a right to seek reimbursement? The Hanafi school says no—such payment is treated as a voluntary gift. We'll explore the textual proof from the hadith of Abu Qatada and understand the underlying principle that actions done without a command are non-compensable.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a guarantor paying the debt without the principal's permission. The ruling is that the guarantor cannot recover from the principal (la yarji').
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith of Abu Qatada (Bukhari no. 2295) where the Prophet (peace be upon him) prayed over a deceased after Abu Qatada volunteered to pay the debt. Abu Qatada did not later seek reimbursement from the deceased's estate.
This hadith is ahad (isolated), so its thubut is zanni, but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet accepted Abu Qatada's guarantee without the deceased's permission, and neither the Prophet nor Abu Qatada demanded recovery. This indicates that without permission, the payment is a voluntary act (tabarru'), not a loan or compensable payment.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The ruling is generally agreed upon within the Hanafi school and also by the Shafi'is. Some exceptions exist if the principal later ratifies, but the default is no recourse.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that without permission, the guarantor cannot recover. This is based on the principle that actions without a command are donations.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[1436] (19) وان كفل بغير امره لم يرجع بما يؤدى. اور اگر مکفول عنہ کے حکم کے بغیر کفیل بنا ہو تو نہیں وصول کرے گا وہ جوادا کیا ہو۔ مکفول عنہ کے حکم کے بغیر کفیل بنا ہو تو کفیل نے جتنا ادا کیا ہو وہ مکفول عنہ سے وصول نہیں کرسکتا۔ مکفول عنہ کے حکم کے بغیر بنا ہے تو کفیل ادا کرنے میں تبرع اور احسان کرنے والا ہوا اس لئے وہ مکفول عنہ سے نہیں وصول کر سکتا (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ ابوقتادہ میت کے حکم کے بغیر کفیل بنے تو بعد میں میت سے وصول نہیں کیا۔ عن سلمة بن الأكوع ان النبي ، اتى بجنازة ليصلى عليها فقال هل عليه من دين ؟ فقالوا لا فصلى عليه ، ثم اتى بجنازة اخرى فقال هل عليه من دين ؟ قالوا نعم قال فصلوا على صاحبكم قال ابو قتادة على دينه يا رسول الله فصلى عليه ( ب ) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من تكفل عن میت دینا فلیس لہ ان مرجع ص ۳۰۶۱ نمبر ۲۲۹۵) اس حدیث میں حضرت ابو قتادہ نے میت سے ادا کیا ہوا دین وصول نہیں کیا۔ کیونکہ بغیر اس کے حکم کے کفیل بنے تھے اصول آمر کے حکم کے بغیر کوئی کام کرنا تبرع اور احسان ہے اس لئے کسی سے اس کا بدلہ وصول نہیں کر سکتا۔ اسی اصول پر یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے۔
[1436] (19) And if he becomes surety without his command, he does not recover what he pays. And if the guarantor was made without the command of the principal, then he will not collect what he paid. If he becomes guarantor without the principal's permission, then the guarantor's payment is a voluntary act and a favor, so he cannot collect from the principal. (2) In a hadith, Abu Qatada became guarantor for a deceased without his command, then he did not recover the debt paid from the deceased. From Salamah ibn al-Akwa' that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was brought a funeral to pray over... he said: 'Is there any debt upon him?' They said, 'No,' so he prayed. Then another funeral was brought, and he said, 'Is there any debt upon him?' They said, 'Yes.' He said, 'Pray for your companion.' Abu Qatada said, 'His debt is upon me, O Messenger of Allah,' so he prayed over him. (Bukhari, chapter on whoever becomes guarantor for a deceased's debt, no. 2295) In this hadith, Abu Qatada did not collect the debt paid from the deceased because he became guarantor without his command. The principle: Doing something without the command of the one commanded is a voluntary gift and favor, so one cannot claim compensation from anyone. This ruling is derived from this principle.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes that if the guarantor became surety without the permission of the principal, he has no right to recover from the principal what he paid. The payment is considered a voluntary act (tabarru') and a favor (ihsan). The evidence is the hadith of Abu Qatada, who guaranteed the debt of a deceased person without the deceased's permission and did not seek reimbursement from the deceased's estate. The underlying usul principle is that actions done without a command are deemed donations, not compensable transactions. This distinguishes it from the previous case where permission was given.

Key Terms
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary act of charity or donation without expectation of compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the guarantor not recover from the principal when he paid without permission?
A) Because the debt was already invalid
B) Because the payment is considered a voluntary donation
C) Because the principal did not authorize the payment
D) Because the hadith forbids recovery in all cases

Key Takeaway
Without the principal's command, a guarantor's payment is a donation, not a compensable loan.

Guarantor Cannot Demand Payment Before Paying
Prohibits pre-payment demand by guarantor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a guarantor may demand reimbursement from the principal and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
The guarantor's right to reimbursement only arises after actual payment, not before.

This passage addresses a key principle in kafalah (suretyship). The guarantor (kafil) cannot demand the money from the principal (makful anhu) before he himself has paid the creditor. This prevents unjust enrichment and ensures the guarantor only claims after bearing the loss. The ruling is a straightforward prohibition based on the condition that the guarantor must first discharge the liability.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the guarantor demanding payment from the principal before paying the creditor. The ruling is that it is not permissible (haram).
2
Identify the condition for permissibility
The condition is that the guarantor must have already paid the debt to the creditor. The demand is only allowed after actual payment.
This condition is explicit in the text: 'before he pays on his behalf'.
3
Understand the rationale
The guarantor has not suffered any loss yet; demanding reimbursement before payment would be akin to seeking compensation without incurring liability. The right to recourse is tied to actual payment.
Other schools may differ, but Hanafis emphasize actual payment.
4
Note the consequence of violation
If the guarantor demands before paying, the demand is invalid and not enforceable. The principal is not obliged to pay until the guarantor has paid.
The text says 'it is not allowed' implying the demand has no legal effect.

The commentary here is incomplete in the given window, but the principle is clear: the guarantor must first discharge the liability before seeking recourse.

Surety's Right of Recourse: Command Required
States the ruling on whether a surety can recover from the principal debtor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a surety can recover from the principal debtor and identify the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Without the principal's command, the surety's payment is a donation — no recovery.

This lesson examines a key distinction in Hanafi kafalah law: whether a surety who pays the debt can later claim reimbursement from the principal debtor. The answer depends entirely on whether the surety acted by the principal's command. We will explore the rule, its underlying principle, and the hadith evidence that establishes it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the surety paying the debt. The ruling: if by the principal's command, the surety recovers; if without command, he does not.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Abu Qatada from Bukhari (no. 2295) is the proof.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Abu Qatada volunteered to pay the deceased's debt without the deceased's command, and the Prophet later did not allow him to recover, showing that without command it is a donation.
The Prophet's silence on recovery is evidence.
4
Identify the underlying principle
Any act done without the principal's authorization is a donation (tabarru'), not a loan or agency, so no recourse.
This is a general principle in Hanafi law.
5
Apply to the general case
This principle applies to all suretyship: the surety must have had the principal's command to recover.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۳۶) بامره رجع بما يؤدى عليه وان فعل بغير امره لم يرجع بما يؤدى

[۱۴] (۱۹) اور اگر مکفول عنہ کے حکم کے بغیر کفیل بنا ہو تو نہیں وصول کرے گا وہ جوادا کیا ہو۔
الشرح مکفول عنہ کے حکم کے بغیر کفیل بنا ہو تو کفیل نے جتنا ادا کیا ہو وہ مکفول عنہ سے وصول نہیں کرسکتا۔ مکفول عنہ کے حکم کے بغیر بنا ہے تو کفیل ادا کرنے میں تبرع اور احسان کرنے والا ہوا اس لئے وہ مکفول عنہ سے نہیں وصول کر سکتا (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ ابوقتادہ میت کے حکم کے بغیر کفیل بنے تو بعد میں میت سے وصول نہیں کیا۔ عن سلمة بن الأكوع ان النبي ، اتى بجنازة ليصلى عليها فقال هل عليه من دين ؟ فقالوا لا فصلى عليه ، ثم اتى بجنازة اخرى فقال هل عليه من دين ؟ قالوا نعم قال فصلوا على صاحبكم قال ابو قتادة على دينه يا رسول الله فصلى عليه ( ب ) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من تكفل عن میت دینا فلیس لہ ان مرجع ص ۳۰۶۱ نمبر ۲۲۹۵) اس حدیث میں حضرت ابو قتادہ نے میت سے ادا کیا ہوا دین وصول نہیں کیا۔ کیونکہ بغیر اس کے حکم کے کفیل بنے تھے اصول آمر کے حکم کے بغیر کوئی کام کرنا تبرع اور احسان ہے اس لئے کسی سے اس کا بدلہ وصول نہیں کر سکتا۔ اسی اصول پر یہ مسئلہ متفرع ہے۔
If by his command, he recovers what he pays; and if he does without his command, he does not recover what he pays. [14] (19) And if he becomes a surety without the command of the principal debtor, he will not recover whatever he has paid. Explanation: If he becomes a surety without the command of the principal debtor, the surety cannot recover from the principal debtor whatever he has paid. Because when he becomes surety without the principal's command, he is a donor and benefactor, so he cannot recover from the principal debtor. (2) There is a hadith that Abu Qatada became a surety for a deceased without his command, and later did not recover the debt from the deceased. From Salamah ibn al-Akwa' that the Prophet (peace be upon him) was brought a funeral to pray over, and he asked, 'Is there any debt upon him?' They said no, so he prayed. Then another funeral was brought, and he asked, 'Is there any debt upon him?' They said yes. He said, 'Pray for your companion.' Abu Qatada said, 'His debt is upon me, O Messenger of Allah.' Then he prayed. (Bukhari, chapter: Whoever becomes surety for a deceased's debt, he has no right to claim it back, no. 2295) In this hadith, Abu Qatada did not recover the debt he paid from the deceased because he became surety without his command. The principle: doing something without the command of the principal is a donation and favor, so one cannot demand its compensation from anyone. This ruling is derived from this principle.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school. It opens by stating the ruling: a surety who pays a debt by the command of the principal debtor may recover that amount from the principal; if he pays without the principal's command, he cannot recover. The commentary explains that without command, the payment is considered a donation (tabarru') and an act of kindness (ihsan), so the surety has no right to reclaim it from the principal. The proof is a hadith of Abu Qatada, who volunteered to pay the debt of a deceased person without the deceased's prior command, and when he later tried to recover, the Prophet did not permit it. This establishes that without explicit command, the surety's payment is a gratuitous transfer. The text emphasizes that the same principle applies to all similar situations: any act done without the principal's authorization is a donation, not a loan or agency.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafil): The surety who guarantees payment of a debt.
مكفول عنه (makful anhu): The principal debtor on whose behalf the surety guarantees.
تبرع (tabarru'): A voluntary act of donation without expectation of compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A surety can only recover from the principal if he paid by the principal's command; otherwise it is a donation.

Kafalah — Surety
intermediate
8 min
Surety Cannot Demand Payment Before Paying
Ruling on the surety's right to demand payment from the principal before paying the debt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a surety can demand reimbursement from the principal debtor and explain the proof from the hadith of the man who paid three dirhams.

Core Idea
A surety's right to reimbursement arises only after he has paid the debt, not before.

This lesson clarifies a key Hanafi principle in the contract of surety (kafalah). The passage from Al-Hidayah states that a surety cannot demand payment from the principal debtor until he himself has paid the creditor. It also addresses a second scenario: if the surety is harassed by the creditor, he may shift that harassment onto the principal. The ruling is derived from the incident where a man paid three dirhams by the Prophet’s command and then recovered from him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage rules upon: the surety's demand for reimbursement. The hukm is that it is not permissible (lā yajūz) for the surety to demand the money from the principal before the surety pays.
The ruling is about legal capacity, not a prohibition in the sense of sin; the surety simply has no right to demand.
2
Locate the proof (dalil)
The commentary refers to a specific incident: a man paid three dirhams by the Prophet’s command and then recovered from the Prophet himself. Identify this as the proof used to establish the principle that payment must precede the right of recourse.
The hadith is from Bayhaqi. The exact wording is not quoted, but the principle is extracted.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
How does the incident prove the ruling? The man paid first (by command), then recovered. This shows that the right to recover is contingent on prior payment. Thus, the surety must pay first before he can demand reimbursement.
This is a clear case of qiyas jali (evident analogy): the surety is like the man who paid, and the principal is like the one from whom he recovered.
4
Distinguish the two rulings in the passage
The passage contains two distinct rulings: (1) the surety cannot demand before paying; (2) if the surety is pursued by the creditor, he may pursue the principal. The second ruling is a separate right arising from the harm suffered by the surety.
The second right is not dependent on prior payment; it is a right to shift the burden of pursuit.
5
Note the exception and voluntary payment
The passage mentions that if the principal voluntarily pays the surety before the surety pays the creditor, it is allowed (jā'iz). This is not a legal demand but a voluntary act.
This exception preserves the possibility of the principal voluntarily reimbursing the surety even before the surety pays.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وليس للكفيل ان يطالب المكفول عنه بالمال قبل ان يؤدى عنه فان لوزم بالمال للكفيل كان له ان يلازم المكفول عنه حتى يخلصه (١٤٣٧)

[۱۴۳۷] (۲۰) کفیل کے لئے جائز نہیں ہے کہ مکفول عنہ سے مال کا مطالبہ کرے اس سے پہلے کہ اپنی جانب سے ادا کرے، پس اگر پیچھا کیا گیا کفیل مال کی وجہ سے تو اس کے لئے حق ہے کہ پیچھا کرے مکفول عنہ کا یہاں تک کہ کفیل کو چھڑا دے۔ اس عبارت میں دو سکتے ہیں ایک تو یہ ہے کہ کفیل جب تک اپنی جانب سے مکفول عنہ کا قرض ادانہ کردے اس وقت تک قانونی طور پر مکفول عنہ سے رقم وصول کرنے کا حقدار نہیں ہوتا۔ ہاں ! مکفول عنہ اپنی مرضی سے کفیل کو رقم دیدے تو جائز ہے۔ مکفول عنہ اصل مقروض ہے اس لئے زیادہ امکان یہی ہے کہ وہ خود قرض ادا کرے گا اور جب وہ خود قرض ادا کرے گا تو کفیل کو اس سے لینے کا حق کیسے ہوگا ؟ ہاں کفیل ادا کر چکا ہو تو اب قرض وصول کرنے والا کفیل ہو گیا اس لئے اب کفیل مکفول عنہ سے لے سکتا ہے (۲) اوپر کی حدیث بیھقی میں آدمی نے حضور کے کہنے پر تین درہم دیا تھا تب جا کر حضور سے وصول کیا۔ صول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ پہلے ادا کرے گا تب وصول کرنے کا حقدار ہوگا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مکفول عنہ کے قرض کی وجہ سے کفیل کوکوئی مصیبت آئی مثلا مکول رہنے کفیل کا پیچھا کیا توکلی کو مکفول عنہ کے ساتھ اتنا کرنے کا حق ہے یعنی مکفول عنہ کا پیچھا کرنے کا حق ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ ملکول عنہ کفیل کے پیچھا کرنے سے اس کو چھڑا نہ لے۔ کفیل کو مکفول عنہ کی وجہ سے پریشانی ہوئی ہے اس لئے وہ یہ پریشانی مکفول عنہ پر ڈال سکتا ہے۔ یلازم : پیچھا کرنا ، ساتھ ساتھ لگے رہنا۔ تخلص چھٹکارا دلانا۔
And it is not for the surety to demand the principal debtor for payment before he pays on his behalf; so if he (the surety) is pursued for the money, the surety has the right to pursue the principal debtor until he releases him. (1437) [1437] (20) It is not permissible for the surety to demand the money from the principal debtor before he pays himself. So if the surety is pursued for the money, he has the right to pursue the principal debtor until he releases him. In this expression, there are two aspects: one is that the surety is not legally entitled to collect the amount from the principal debtor until he pays the debt himself. However, if the principal voluntarily gives the money to the surety, it is permissible. The principal is the original debtor, so it is more likely that he will pay himself; if he pays himself, how can the surety have the right to take from him? Yes, if the surety has paid, then the surety becomes the one entitled to receive the debt, so now the surety can take from the principal. (2) The hadith above (from Bayhaqi) about the man who gave three dirhams by the Prophet's command, then he recovered from the Prophet. This ruling is based on the principle that first he pays, then he becomes entitled to recover. The second issue is that if the surety faces trouble due to the principal's debt, e.g., he is pursued, then the surety has the right to pursue the principal until the principal releases him from the pursuit. The surety suffered trouble because of the principal, so he can shift that trouble onto the principal. Yulazimu: to pursue, to stay with. Takhlis: to get free.
Source pages p. 313

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling and its rationale from the Hanafi school. It states that a surety cannot demand payment from the principal debtor before the surety himself pays the creditor. The reason is that the surety's right to reimbursement arises only after he has discharged the debt; until then, the principal is still the primary debtor. However, if the principal voluntarily pays the surety, it is allowed. The passage also addresses a second scenario: if the surety is pursued by the creditor, he has the right to pursue the principal debtor in turn, effectively shifting the burden of harassment. The commentary explains the principle: one who pays first becomes entitled to collect; one who suffers inconvenience due to another can pass that inconvenience back. The hadith from Bayhaqi (mentioned earlier) supports that the surety can recover only after paying by command.

Key Terms
لوزم (luzima): To be pursued or held liable for payment.
يلازم (yulazimu): To persistently pursue or stay with someone.
تخلص (takhlis): To get released or freed from a claim or pursuit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the surety have the right to demand reimbursement from the principal debtor?
A) Immediately after becoming surety
B) After the surety has paid the debt to the creditor
C) Only if the principal debtor is insolvent
D) Never, it is a donation

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a surety's right to reimbursement is contingent on actual payment of the debt, but if the surety is pursued by the creditor, he may pursue the principal even before paying.

Release of Surety by Ibra' or Istifa'
States that the surety is released if the creditor releases the principal or receives payment from him.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the discharge of a surety when the principal debtor is released or pays, and explain the legal basis (the asl-far' principle).

Core Idea
The surety's obligation is subsidiary—when the principal debt ends, the surety is automatically freed.

This lesson examines a key rule in Hanafi kafalah: the effect of the creditor's actions on the surety. Understanding this principle reinforces the hierarchical relationship between primary and accessory obligations in Islamic law. The ruling is clear: if the creditor releases the principal debtor or receives full payment from him, the surety is released automatically, because the surety's obligation is merely an accessory to the principal debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Identify the legal act being discussed: the release of the surety from his obligation. The ruling states that the surety is released in two specific scenarios.
The ruling is about the discharge of the surety, not about formation of the kafalah.
2
Distinguish the two triggering events
Note the two ways the principal debt can be extinguished: either by the creditor's unilateral release (ibra') or by the principal's payment (istifa'). Both lead to the same result for the surety.
Ibra' is a unilateral act by the creditor; istifa' requires the principal debtor's action.
3
Trace the legal reasoning (asl-far')
Understand the commentary: the surety is a branch (far') of the principal debtor. Since the principal is the original source of the debt, when the principal obligation ends, the accessory obligation of the surety automatically ends.
This uses the Hanafi maxim that the subsidiary follows the principal.
4
Identify the underlying principle
Generalize: the ruling is based on the principle that extinguishing the principal obligation extinguishes all accessories. This applies to other accessory obligations in fiqh.
This principle is not limited to kafalah; e.g., a pledged item may be released upon debt payment.
5
Apply to a hypothetical
Test yourself: if Zaid owes Amr 1000 dirhams and Bakr is surety, and Amr tells Zaid 'I forgive your debt', what happens to Bakr? Answer: Bakr is released.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا ابرأ الطالب المكفول عنه او استوفى منه برئ الكفيل

[۱۴۳۸] (۲۱) اگر طالب نے مکفول عنہ کو بری کر دیا یا اس سے وصول کر لیا تو کفیل بری ہو جائے گا۔
الشرح اصل میں قرض تو مکفول عنہ پر ہے۔ کفیل تو فرع ہے اور اس سے مستفاد ہے۔ اس لئے مکفول لہ دائن نے مکفول عنہ مقروض کو دین سے بری کرد یا یا معاف کرد یایا دوسری شکل ہے کہ خود مکفول عنہ نے اپنادین ادا کر دیا تو چونکہ اصل پر دین نہیں رہا اس لئے کفیل جو فرع ہے اس پر بھی دین نہیں رہے گا اور ختم ہو جائے گا ہاں یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اصل پر دین نہ رہے تو فرع سے بھی دین ختم ہو جائے گا۔ استونی : وفی سے مشتق ہے، وصول کر لیا۔
And if the creditor releases the principal debtor or receives payment from him, the surety is released. [1438] (21) If the creditor releases the principal debtor or receives payment from him, the surety will be released. Explanation: Actually, the debt is upon the principal debtor. The surety is a branch and derived from him. Therefore, if the creditor releases the principal debtor from the debt, or forgives it, or if the principal debtor pays his debt himself, then since the debt no longer remains on the principal, the surety who is a branch will also no longer have the debt upon him, and it will be cancelled. Yes, this ruling is based on the principle that when the debt no longer remains on the principal, it ends from the branch as well. Istawfa: derived from wafa, meaning he received payment.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage states a straightforward ruling from the Hanafi school: the surety is released from the obligation if the creditor releases the principal debtor (i.e., forgives the debt) or if the principal debtor pays the debt directly. The commentary explains the legal reasoning: the surety's obligation is subsidiary (far') to the principal debtor's obligation (asl). Since the surety is merely a guarantor, once the principal obligation is extinguished—whether by release (ibra') or payment (istifa')—the accessory obligation of the surety automatically falls away. This is based on the general legal maxim that the subsidiary follows the principal. The text also glosses the word 'istawfa' as meaning he received the full payment.

Key Terms
إبراء (ibra'): Release or discharge from a debt by the creditor.
استيفاء (istifa'): Receiving full payment of a debt.
فرع (far'): That which is subsidiary or derived from something else; here the surety's obligation is far' to the principal's debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens to the surety's obligation when the creditor releases the principal debtor?
A) The surety becomes the primary debtor
B) The surety is also released
C) The surety remains liable
D) The surety must pay immediately

Key Takeaway
The surety's obligation is accessory; extinguishing the principal debt automatically frees the surety.

Release of Surety Does Not Release Principal
Explains that releasing the surety does not discharge the principal debtor.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between two types of release (ibra') in kafalah and state the effect on the principal debtor.

Core Idea
Releasing the surety does not release the principal – unless the debt itself is forgiven.

In this lesson, you will examine a key distinction in Hanafi suretyship law. The passage clarifies that the effect of releasing a surety depends on whether the creditor forgives the debt itself or merely releases the surety from the obligation to pay. Understanding this difference is essential for correctly applying rulings in guarantee contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Read the passage and note two ways a creditor can release a surety: by forgiving the debt itself or by releasing only from suretyship.
2
Distinguish the legal effect
For each scenario, determine whether the principal debtor is released. The first scenario extinguishes the debt for both; the second leaves the principal liable.
The key is what the creditor intends and states.
3
Understand the rationale
If the debt itself is forgiven, the underlying obligation ceases, freeing both surety and principal. If only the suretyship is waived, the principal's debt remains intact – the creditor simply gave up recourse against the surety.
4
Apply to a new case
Suppose the creditor says to the surety, 'I am not going to ask you for the money.' Is the principal liable? Apply the rule: this is release from suretyship only, so the principal still owes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ابرأ الكفيل لم يبرأ المكفول عنه

[۱۴۳۹ (۲۲) اگر کفیل کو بری کر دیا تو مکفول عنہ بری نہیں ہوگا۔
الشرح بری کرنے کی دو صورتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ اصل دین ہی کفیل سے معاف کر دیا تو اس صورت میں مکفول عنہ سے بھی معاف ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اصل دین ہی اصیل سے معاف ہو گیا۔ اور دوسری صورت یہ ہے کہ کفیل کو صرف کفالت سے بری کیا کہ اب میں آپ سے دین کا مطالبہ نہیں کروں گا۔ اس صورت میں چونکہ اصل دین اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ پر باقی ہے اس لئے اصیل یعنی مکفول عنہ مطالبہ سے بری نہیں ہو گا۔ مکفول لہ اس سے دین کا مطالبہ کر سکتا ہے۔
And if he releases the surety, the principal debtor is not released. [1439] (22) If the surety is released, the principal debtor will not be released. Explanation: There are two forms of release. One is that the original debt itself is forgiven to the surety; in that case, it will also be forgiven to the principal debtor because the original debt has been forgiven from the original debtor. The second form is that the surety is only released from the suretyship, meaning 'I will not demand the debt from you.' In this case, since the original debt remains upon the principal debtor, the principal debtor is not released from the demand; the creditor can demand from him.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage presents the complementary ruling to the previous one: releasing the surety does not automatically release the principal debtor. The commentary explains two scenarios. First, if the creditor forgives the debt itself to the surety (i.e., declares the debt canceled for everyone), then both surety and principal are released because the debt is extinguished. Second, if the creditor only releases the surety from the obligation of suretyship (i.e., promises not to pursue the surety), the principal's debt remains intact because the release is personal to the surety. The creditor can still demand payment from the principal. This distinction hinges on whether the release is of the debt itself (ibra' 'an al-dayn) or of the suretyship (ibra' 'an al-kafalah).

Key Terms
إبراء الكفيل (ibra' al-kafil): Release of the surety from his obligation; may be either from the debt itself or from the suretyship.
أصيل (asil): The original debtor, i.e., the principal debtor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the creditor tells the surety, 'I release you from the suretyship and will not demand from you,' what is the effect on the principal debtor?
A) The principal debtor is also released
B) The principal debtor remains liable
C) The debt is halved
D) The surety becomes the principal debtor

Key Takeaway
Releasing the surety does not release the principal debtor unless the release expressly forgives the underlying debt.

Surety's Right to Pursue the Principal Debtor After Payment
Ruling on surety's right to pursue principal debtor until release

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on when a surety may demand reimbursement from the principal debtor and apply the condition that prior payment by the surety is required.

Core Idea
A surety cannot reclaim from the debtor until he has paid the creditor himself.

In the chapter of suretyship (kafalah), a key question is: when can the surety (kafil) turn to the principal debtor (makful 'anhu) for reimbursement? The classical Hanafi text clarifies that the surety's right to pursue the debtor is conditional upon having first discharged the debt. This lesson unpacks that ruling and its proof from a hadith in Sunan al-Bayhaqi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the surety pursuing the principal debtor for reimbursement. The ruling is that it is permissible (mubah) but with a condition: the surety must have paid the creditor first.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites a hadith from Bayhaqi: a man gave three dirhams upon the Prophet's instruction, then went and collected from the Prophet. This shows the sequence.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key point is the order: payment before collection. The man gave first, then collected. This indicates that the surety must pay before seeking reimbursement.
The imperative is not explicit but the implied sequence is used as proof.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools may allow the surety to demand reimbursement immediately upon becoming surety, without prior payment. The Hanafi school insists on prior payment.
This difference is legitimate (mukhtalaf fih).
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi position is considered stronger because it follows the apparent meaning of the hadith and avoids potential injustice to the debtor.
The mufta bihi is that the surety must pay first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالمال للكفيل كان له ان يلازم المكفول عنه حتى يخلصه [ ۱۴۳۸] (۲۱) واذا ابرأ الطالب المكفول عنه او استوفى منه برئ الكفيل [۱۴۳۹ (۲۲) وان ابرأ الكفيل لم يبرأ المكفول عنه.
گیا کفیل مال کی وجہ سے تو اس کے لئے حق ہے کہ پیچھا کرے مکفول عنہ کا یہاں تک کہ کفیل کو چھڑا دے۔ اس عبارت میں دو سکتے ہیں ایک تو یہ ہے کہ کفیل جب تک اپنی جانب سے مکفول عنہ کا قرض ادانہ کردے اس وقت تک قانونی طور پر مکفول عنہ سے رقم وصول کرنے کا حقدار نہیں ہوتا۔ ہاں ! مکفول عنہ اپنی مرضی سے کفیل کو رقم دیدے تو جائز ہے۔ مکفول عنہ اصل مقروض ہے اس لئے زیادہ امکان یہی ہے کہ وہ خود قرض ادا کرے گا اور جب وہ خود قرض ادا کرے گا تو کفیل کو اس سے لینے کا حق کیسے ہوگا ؟ ہاں کفیل ادا کر چکا ہو تو اب قرض وصول کرنے والا کفیل ہو گیا اس لئے اب کفیل مکفول عنہ سے لے سکتا ہے (۲) اوپر کی حدیث بیھقی میں آدمی نے حضور کے کہنے پر تین درہم دیا تھا تب جا کر حضور سے وصول کیا۔
صول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ پہلے ادا کرے گا تب وصول کرنے کا حقدار ہوگا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مکفول عنہ کے قرض کی وجہ سے کفیل کوکوئی مصیبت آئی مثلا مکول رہنے کفیل کا پیچھا کیا توکلی کو مکفول عنہ کے ساتھ اتنا کرنے کا حق ہے یعنی مکفول عنہ کا پیچھا کرنے کا حق ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ ملکول عنہ کفیل کے پیچھا کرنے سے اس کو چھڑا نہ لے۔ کفیل کو مکفول عنہ کی وجہ سے پریشانی ہوئی ہے اس لئے وہ یہ پریشانی مکفول عنہ پر ڈال سکتا ہے۔
یلازم : پیچھا کرنا ، ساتھ ساتھ لگے رہنا۔ تخلص چھٹکارا دلانا۔
For the surety by wealth, he has the right to pursue the principal debtor until he releases him. [1438] (21) And if the claimant discharges the principal debtor or collects from him, the surety is discharged. [1439] (22) And if he discharges the surety, the principal debtor is not discharged. The surety by wealth has the right to pursue the principal debtor until he releases him. In this phrase there are two aspects: one is that the surety, as long as he does not pay the debt of the principal debtor from his side, is not legally entitled to collect the amount from the principal debtor. However, if the principal debtor voluntarily gives the amount to the surety, it is permissible. The principal debtor is the original debtor, so it is most likely that he himself will pay the debt. And when he himself pays the debt, how can the surety have the right to take from him? Yes, if the surety has already paid, then he becomes the one collecting the debt, so now the surety can take from the principal debtor. (2) The above hadith in Bayhaqi: a man gave three dirhams upon the Prophet's instruction, then went and collected from the Prophet. The principle of this issue is that first he will pay, then he will be entitled to collect. The second issue is that if the surety suffers any trouble due to the debt of the principal debtor, e.g., the principal debtor was pursued, the surety has the right to do so with the principal debtor, i.e., to pursue the principal debtor until the principal debtor releases him from his pursuit. The surety has been troubled because of the principal debtor, so he can place this trouble on the principal debtor. يلازم: to pursue, to stick with. تخلص: to release.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter of suretyship (kafalah) along with its commentary. The author presents the ruling that a surety who has paid a debt has the right to pursue the principal debtor to recover what he paid. The commentary explains two aspects: first, the surety cannot demand payment from the principal debtor until he himself has actually paid the creditor; second, if the surety suffers harassment from the creditor for the debt, he can transfer that harassment to the principal debtor by pursuing him. The hadith from Bayhaqi illustrates the principle that the surety must pay first before collecting. The Urdu commentary also clarifies the legal terminology.

Key Terms
كفيل (kafil): The person who becomes a surety/guarantor for a debt or obligation.
مكفول عنه (makful anhu): The principal debtor on whose behalf the surety is given.
طالب (talib): The creditor who demands payment (the beneficiary of the suretyship).
يلازم (yulazim): To pursue or stick with someone, referring to the surety's right to chase the debtor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view, when does the surety gain the right to demand reimbursement from the principal debtor?
A) Immediately upon becoming surety
B) Only after he has paid the creditor
C) When the creditor demands payment
D) After a court order

Key Takeaway
The surety's right to pursue the debtor is conditional on prior payment; until he pays, he cannot legally demand reimbursement.

Discharge of Surety Upon Creditor's Action
Ruling on automatic discharge of surety

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two acts of the creditor that automatically discharge the surety and explain the legal principle (far' follows asl) that underlies this ruling.

Core Idea
If the debt on the principal debtor ends, the surety's obligation ends automatically.

This passage presents a straightforward but foundational rule in the law of suretyship (kafalah). When the creditor either releases the principal debtor from the debt or receives payment from him, the surety is freed from liability. The commentary explains the rationale: the surety's obligation is a subsidiary branch (far') that depends on the principal (asl). Understanding this principle helps clarify many related issues in kafalah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two triggering events
The passage mentions two actions by the creditor that discharge the surety: discharging (ibra') the principal debtor and collecting (istawfa) from him. Note that collection can be direct payment by the debtor or other means.
2
Understand the principal–branch relationship
The commentary states that the surety is a branch (far') and the principal debtor is the origin (asl). The debt is fundamentally on the principal debtor; the surety is only a backer.
3
Apply the principle: termination of origin terminates branch
Because the debt on the principal is extinguished (by discharge or payment), the subsidiary obligation of the surety must also end.
4
Distinguish from cases where the creditor releases the surety directly
This passage is about the creditor's action toward the principal debtor; if the creditor releases the surety directly, that also discharges the surety, but that is a separate ruling.
The discharge here is automatic without separate action by the surety.
5
Note the universal application
The ruling applies to all types of suretyship (kafalah bi al-dayn) and is agreed upon by the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا ابرأ الطالب المكفول عنه او استوفى منه برئ الكفيل
[۱۴۳۸] (۲۱) اگر طالب نے مکفول عنہ کو بری کر دیا یا اس سے وصول کر لیا تو کفیل بری ہو جائے گا۔
اصل میں قرض تو مکفول عنہ پر ہے۔ کفیل تو فرع ہے اور اس سے مستفاد ہے۔ اس لئے مکفول لہ دائن نے مکفول عنہ مقروض کو دین سے بری کرد یا یا معاف کرد یایا دوسری شکل ہے کہ خود مکفول عنہ نے اپنادین ادا کر دیا تو چونکہ اصل پر دین نہیں رہا اس لئے کفیل جو فرع ہے اس پر بھی دین نہیں رہے گا اور ختم ہو جائے گا ہاں یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ اصل پر دین نہ رہے تو فرع سے بھی دین ختم ہو جائے گا۔
استونی : وفی سے مشتق ہے، وصول کر لیا۔
And if the claimant discharges the principal debtor or collects from him, the surety is discharged. [1438] (21) If the claimant discharged the principal debtor or collected from him, the surety will be discharged. In reality, the debt is on the principal debtor. The surety is a branch and derives from him. Therefore, when the creditor discharged the principal debtor from the debt or forgave it, or the other form that the principal debtor himself paid his debt, then since the debt no longer remains on the principal, the surety who is a branch will also have no debt and it will be terminated. Yes, this issue is based on the principle that when the debt on the principal is terminated, the debt on the branch is also terminated. استونی: derived from وفی, meaning collected.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This is a ruling on the termination of suretyship. The author states that if the creditor (talib) either releases the principal debtor (makful anhu) from the debt or collects the debt from him, then the surety (kafil) is automatically discharged. The commentary explains the reason: the principal debtor is the original obligor, and the surety is only a subsidiary (far'). Since the debt on the principal is extinguished, the subsidiary obligation also vanishes. This is compared to the principle that if the original debt is removed, the guarantee is removed.

Key Terms
ابرأ (abra'a): To discharge or release someone from a debt.
استوفى (istawfa): To collect or receive payment in full.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the creditor collects the debt from the principal debtor, what happens to the surety?
A) The surety remains liable until explicitly released
B) The surety is discharged automatically
C) The surety becomes jointly liable with the debtor
D) The surety must still pay half

Key Takeaway
The surety's obligation automatically ends when the debt on the principal debtor is extinguished, whether by discharge or payment.

Conditional Discharge from Suretyship: The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on conditional discharge of suretyship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi views on suspending the discharge of suretyship upon a condition, and identify the mufta bihi position with its evidence.

Core Idea
Discharging a surety is dropping a claim, not transferring ownership, so conditional discharge is valid.

In Hanafi fiqh, kafalah (suretyship) creates a right of recourse against the surety. A creditor may wish to conditionally discharge the surety—for example, upon arrival of a third party. Is such a conditional discharge valid? The Hanafi school has two views rooted in the nature of the surety's liability. This lesson unpacks the disagreement and the preferred position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the dispute is about whether ta'liq (suspension) of a discharge (bara'ah) from kafalah upon a condition is valid. The act in question: a creditor tells the surety, 'If tomorrow comes, you are discharged.'
Ta'liq is generally valid in dropping claims but invalid in transferring ownership (tamlik).
2
State the first view and its basis
The primary view (zahir al-riwayah) holds that conditional discharge is invalid. The basis: discharging the surety is akin to making him an owner of his obligation (tamlik), which requires immediacy.
Abu Hanifa's position as recorded in the primary narrations.
3
State the second view and its basis
A second narration (from Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) holds that conditional discharge is valid. The basis: the surety does not owe the original debt; only a right of claim exists. Therefore, discharge is merely dropping a claim, which can be suspended on a condition.
This view relies on the distinction between tamlik and isqat (dropping).
4
Identify the mufta bihi and the tarjih
The commentary states that the fatwa is on the second view. The later Hanafi masters preferred it, and it is the operative ruling for practice.
Tarjih authority: 'upon this is the fatwa'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز تعليق البراءة من الكفالة بشرط [۱۴۴۰] (۲۳) کفالت سے برأت کو شرط کے ساتھ معلق کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مکفول لہ کفیل کو کسی شرط پر معلق کر کے بری کرنا چاہے تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلا یوں کہے کہ کل آئے گا تو آپ کفالت سے بری ہیں یہ سیح
نہیں ہے۔
کفالت سے بری کرنا گویا کہ مالک بنانا ہے اور مالک بنانے کو شرط پر معلق کر ناصحیح نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کفالت سے بری کرنے کو شرط پر معلق کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
لیکن دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ برات کو شرط پر معلق کرنا صحیح ہے۔ کفیل پر اصل دین نہیں ہے اس پر تو صرف مطالبہ ہے تو اس سے بری کرنا مالک بناتا نہیں ہے بلکہ مطالبہ ساقط کرنا ہے اس لئے كفالت سے بری کرنے کو کسی مناسب شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز ہے اور اسی پر فتوی ہے۔
And it is not permissible to suspend discharge from suretyship upon a condition. [1440] (23) It is not permissible to suspend discharge from suretyship upon a condition. If the creditor wants to discharge the surety conditionally, it is not permissible. For example, if he says, 'If tomorrow comes, you are discharged from the suretyship,' this is not valid. Releasing from suretyship is like making someone owner, and making someone owner upon a condition is not valid. Therefore, suspending discharge from suretyship upon a condition is not valid. But in another narration, it is said that suspending the discharge upon a condition is valid. The surety does not owe the original debt; upon him is only the claim. So discharging him does not make him an owner but rather removes the claim. Therefore, suspending the discharge from suretyship upon a suitable condition is permissible, and upon this is the fatwa.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This ruling addresses the validity of conditional discharge from suretyship. The primary view (from Abu Hanifa?) states that discharge cannot be suspended on a condition because it is akin to making someone an owner (tamlik), which requires immediate effect. However, a second narration (possibly from Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) considers that since the surety only has a claim upon him (mutalaba) and not the actual debt, discharging him is simply dropping a claim, which can be conditional. The commentary states that the fatwa is on the second view, allowing conditional discharge if the condition is appropriate. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Key Terms
تعليق (ta'liq): Suspending a legal effect upon a future condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the fatwa (mufta bihi) in this lesson, which of the following is true about a creditor saying to the surety, 'If Zaid arrives, you are discharged'?
A) It is invalid because ta'liq is not allowed in kafalah.
B) It is valid because discharging a surety is dropping a claim.
C) It is invalid because the condition is not suitable.
D) It is valid only if the surety agrees in writing.

Key Takeaway
Conditional discharge from suretyship is valid in the Hanafi school (mufta bihi) because it is dropping a claim, not transferring ownership.

The Invalidity of Suretyship for Hudud and Qisas
Ruling with proof on invalidity of kafalah for hudud and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that suretyship for hudud and qisas is invalid and explain the rationale based on the non-transferability of these punishments.

Core Idea
Punishments like hudud and qisas cannot be transferred to a surety.

In financial transactions, suretyship is a common way to guarantee an obligation. But can you become surety for a punishment? This passage clarifies that hudud (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation) are personal to the offender and cannot be assumed by a third party. We will examine the ruling, its supporting evidence, and the distinction between this and other forms of suretyship.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the principle: any right that cannot be exacted from the surety renders suretyship invalid. Here, hudud and qisas are given as examples.
The term 'right' (haqq) is used broadly; these are rights of Allah or personal rights of the victim.
2
Understand the rationale
Analyze why these punishments cannot be transferred: they are specific to the actual offender and cannot be executed on a substitute.
This contrasts with financial debts, which can be collected from the surety.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd' is cited. Determine its implications for the ruling.
Although the hadith is ahad and zanni in transmission, it is accepted in this context.
4
Distinguish from kafalah bil-nafs
Note the difference: previous ruling prohibited forcing someone to act as surety for the person's appearance; this ruling prohibits becoming surety for the punishment itself.
This helps avoid confusion between two related but distinct issues.

و كل حق لا يمكن استيفاؤه من الكفيل لا تصح الكفالة به كالحدود والقصاص [۱۴۴۱] (۲۴) ہر وہ حق کہ اس کا وصول کرنا کفیل سے ممکن نہ ہو اس کا کفالہ صحیح نہیں ہے ۔ جیسے حدود اور قصاص۔ جو چیز نفیل سے لینا یا وصول کر ناممکن نہیں اس کا کفیل بنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ جیسے کوئی کہے کہ مجرم پر اگر حد جاری نہ کر سکو تو میں اس کا کفیل بنتا ہوں کہ مجھ پر وہ حد جاری کر دیں۔ یا مجرم سے قصاص نہ لے سکو تو میں اس کا کفیل بنتا ہوں کہ مجھ سے قصاص لے لو اور میرا ہا تھ قصاص مین کاٹ دو تو یہ کفیل بنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔
حدود اور قصاص اصل مجرم سے ہی لئے جاتے ہیں دوسروں سے نہیں۔ اس لئے اس کی کفالت بھی درست نہیں ہیں (۲) حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ حدثنی عـمـر بـن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده ان النبي الا الله قال لا كفالة في حد (الف) ( سنن سبیھقی ، باب ماجاء فی الكفالة ببدن من عليه حق ، ج سادس ص ۱۲۷، نمبر ۱۱۴۱۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حد میں کفالت نہیں ہے۔ جس کا ایک مطلب یہ ہے کہ حد کا کوئی کفیل بن جائے کہ مجرم پر نہ کر سکوتو مجھ پر حد جاری کر و تو یہ میچ نہیں ہے۔
وٹ اوپر کے ایک مسئلہ میں تھا کہ حد اور قصاص میں کفالہ بالنفس لینے کے لئے مجبور کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اور یہاں ہے کہ خود حد اور قصاص کا کفیل بننا درست نہیں ہے ۔ اس لئے دونوں مسئلوں میں فرق ہے۔
And every right that cannot be exacted from the surety, suretyship for it is not valid, such as hudud and qisas. [1441] (24) Every right that cannot be collected from the surety, its suretyship is not valid. Like hudud and qisas. A thing that cannot be taken or collected from the surety, making him a surety for it is not valid. For example, if someone says, 'If you cannot execute the hadd on the criminal, then I am surety for it so that you execute the hadd on me,' or 'If you cannot take qisas from the criminal, then I am surety for it so that you take qisas from me and cut off my hand in qisas,' then this suretyship is not valid. Hudud and qisas are taken from the actual criminal, not from others. Therefore, suretyship for them is not valid. (2) The hadith has passed. 'Umar ibn Shu'ayb narrated from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'There is no suretyship in hadd.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on suretyship for the person against whom there is a right, vol. 6, p. 127, no. 11417). In this hadith, there is no suretyship in hadd. One meaning is that someone cannot become a surety for a hadd, saying 'if you cannot execute it on the criminal, then execute it on me,' that is not correct. And note that in a previous issue, it was said that forcing to take kafalah bil-nafs for hadd and qisas is not valid. And here, the suretyship itself for hadd and qisas is not valid. So there is a difference between the two issues.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This ruling states that suretyship is invalid for punishments like hudud (fixed penalties) and qisas (retaliation) because these are personal rights that can only be exacted from the actual offender. The commentary gives examples and supports the ruling with a hadith from Sunan al-Bayhaqi: 'There is no suretyship in hadd.' The commentary also clarifies that this issue is different from a previous ruling about kafalah bil-nafs for bringing the person; that was about compelling the surety to produce the criminal, whereas this is about becoming surety for the punishment itself.

Key Terms
حدود (hudud): Fixed corporal punishments prescribed by Islamic law for specific crimes (e.g., theft, zina).
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for murder or bodily harm, a right of the victim.
كفالة (kafalah): Suretyship; a contract where a third party (kafil) guarantees an obligation or brings a person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the surety might flee
B) Because these punishments are rights that cannot be exacted from anyone other than the actual offender
C) Because hudud require a court order
D) Because qisas is only for intentional acts

Key Takeaway
Suretyship for corporal punishments (hudud and qisas) is invalid because the punishment is personal to the offender and cannot be transferred to a surety.

Suretyship for the Purchase Price (Kafalah al-Thaman)
Ruling on validity of suretyship for purchase price

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling that suretyship for the purchase price is valid and explain why it is treated as a debt suretyship.

Core Idea
Paying the price is a debt; suretyship for debts is always valid.

In this lesson, we examine a short but important ruling: a person can validly guarantee the price that the buyer owes to the seller. This is because the unpaid price is a financial debt, and the Hanafi school recognizes suretyship (kafalah) for all types of debts. The passage clarifies that no special conditions apply to the price – it is simply another debt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Find the exact act being ruled upon: a person becomes a surety for the buyer regarding the purchase price. Note that the ruling is 'jā'iz' (permissible/valid).
The Arabic phrase 'واذا ضمن المشتري الثمن جاز' directly gives the ruling.
2
Extract the legal reasoning (illah)
Look for why this act is valid. The text states: 'Paying the price is also a type of debt.' This is the key reason.
The analogy: since debt suretyship is valid, and price is a debt, then price suretyship is valid.
3
Apply the general principle of kafalah
Connect to the broader Hanafi rule: any known financial debt can be the subject of a valid kafalah. Confirm that the price qualifies.
No special conditions for price other than being a debt.

The text is incomplete; it begins to discuss conditions of the price. Recognize that standard conditions of kafalah (e.g., known amount, consent of parties) apply by default.
The passage cuts off, so we only have the core ruling.

Suspending Release from Kafalah on a Condition
Ruling on suspending discharge from suretyship upon a condition (intra-Hanafi dispute)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on suspending release from kafalah upon a condition and explain why the mufta bihi view allows it.

Core Idea
Discharging a surety is isqat, not tamlik — so it can be conditional.

The passage tackles an intra-Hanafi dispute: can a creditor release a surety contingently? One view, by analogy to tamlik, rules it invalid. The other, relied upon for fatwa, treats it as isqat and permits it. Understanding the difference between tamlik and isqat is key.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The legal act is the creditor suspending the discharge of the surety from kafalah upon a condition (e.g., 'if tomorrow comes, you are released').
2
State the primary transmission
The first transmission (zahir al-riwayah) holds this invalid. The reasoning: discharging a surety is like transferring ownership (tamlik) of the debt to him, and making ownership conditional is invalid.
This view analogises kafalah discharge to a conditional gift.
3
State the second transmission
The second transmission (nawadir, mufta bihi) holds it valid. The reasoning: the surety does not owe the debt itself; he is only subject to mutalabah (right of pursuit). Discharging him is dropping that right (isqat), which can be validly conditioned.
Thus, the condition does not create ownership but merely waives a claim.
4
Identify the illa (effective cause) of each view
First view illa: kafalah discharge is tamlik. Second view illa: kafalah discharge is isqat of mutalabah.
The illa determines whether conditions are permissible.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text explicitly states 'wa 'alayhi al-fatwa' — the second view is the one upon which fatwa is given. Conditional release is valid provided the condition is appropriate (munasib).
In practice, the surety is released upon fulfillment of the condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يجوز تعليق البراءة من الكفالة بشرط. اصول یہ مسئلہ اس اصول پر ہے کہ کفیل کو کفالت سے بری کرنے سے اصیل سے دین ساقط نہیں ہوگا اور نہ مطالبہ سے بری ہوگا۔ (۱۴۴۰) (۲۳) کفالت سے برأت کو شرط کے ساتھ معلق کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مکفول لہ کفیل کو کسی شرط پر معلق کر کے بری کرنا چاہے تو یہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ مثلا یوں کہے کہ کل آئے گا تو آپ کفالت سے بری ہیں یہ سیح نہیں ہے۔ کفالت سے بری کرنا گویا کہ مالک بنانا ہے اور مالک بنانے کو شرط پر معلق کر ناصحیح نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کفالت سے بری کرنے کو شرط پر معلق کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ لیکن دوسری روایت میں ہے کہ برات کو شرط پر معلق کرنا صحیح ہے۔ کفیل پر اصل دین نہیں ہے اس پر تو صرف مطالبہ ہے تو اس سے بری کرنا مالک بناتا نہیں ہے بلکہ مطالبہ ساقط کرنا ہے اس لئے کفالت سے بری کرنے کو کسی مناسب شرط پر معلق کرنا جائز ہے اور اسی پر فتوی ہے۔
And it is not permissible to suspend release from suretyship upon a condition. The basis of this matter is that releasing the surety from the suretyship does not drop the debt from the principal debtor, nor does it drop the right to pursue. (23) It is not permissible to suspend release from suretyship upon a condition. The creditor (makful lahu) wants to discharge the surety suspended upon a condition, that is not permissible. For example, he says: 'If tomorrow comes, you are released from the suretyship' — this is not valid. Discharging from suretyship is like making the surety owner [of his liability], and making ownership conditional is not valid. Therefore, suspending release from suretyship upon a condition is not valid. However, in another transmission, suspending release upon a condition is valid. The surety does not owe the original debt; he only owes being pursued. So discharging him is not making him owner, but rather dropping the right of pursuit. Therefore, suspending release from suretyship upon an appropriate condition is permissible, and this is the basis for fatwa.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on suspending the discharge of a surety from his suretyship upon a condition. The primary transmission (zahir al-riwayah) holds that such a suspension is invalid because discharging the surety is analogous to transferring ownership (tamlik) of the debt to him; making ownership conditional is invalid. The example given is the creditor saying, 'If tomorrow comes, you are released.' The second, relied-upon transmission (nawadir, mufta bihi) argues that the surety's liability is not a debt but merely the right to pursue him (mutalabah). Discharging him is thus dropping a right (isqat), which can be validly conditional. The text concludes by stating that fatwa is given on the second view, making the conditional discharge valid.

Key Terms
براءة (bara'ah): Release or discharge from the obligation of suretyship.
كفالة (kafalah): Suretyship; a contract where a person (kafil) guarantees the debt or presence of another (makful 'anhu).
شرط (shart): A condition upon which the validity or execution of an act depends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is suspending release from kafalah on a condition considered valid in the mufta bihi view?
A) Because the surety's liability is a debt that can be made conditional.
B) Because the surety's liability is merely the right to pursue him, which is a right that can be dropped conditionally.
C) Because the creditor can always change his mind about releasing the surety.
D) Because the principal debtor has given permission for the condition.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two views on conditional release of a surety; the relied-upon view permits it because it is isqat not tamlik.

Kafalah Invalid for Personal Punishments: Hudud and Qisas
Ruling that kafalah is invalid for non-financial rights like hadd and qisas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that kafalah for hadd and qisas is invalid and explain the dalil from hadith and the rationale that these rights cannot be exacted from the surety.

Core Idea
Kafalah for hadd and qisas is invalid because these punishments are personal to the offender and cannot be transferred.

In this lesson, we examine a specific limitation on the contract of kafalah (suretyship). The general principle is that kafalah is only valid for rights that the surety can fulfill. Hudud (fixed punishments) and qisas (retaliation) are rights that are personal to the original perpetrator; they cannot be executed on a surety. The Hanafi school, citing a hadith, rules that any kafalah for such rights is invalid, even if the surety volunteers. This lesson will guide you through the ruling, its proof, and the underlying rationale.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule and its scope
The passage begins with a maxim: every right that cannot be exacted from the surety, kafalah is invalid. This includes hudud and qisas. Identify that the rule is general but the text specifies these two examples.
2
Examine the example scenario
The text provides an example: someone voluntarily offers to undergo hadd or qisas on behalf of the criminal. The ruling is that such an offer is invalid. Understand why: the right is specific to the criminal.
3
Analyze the dalil: hadith 'La kafalah fi hadd'
The hadith explicitly negates kafalah in matters of hadd. Note that the hadith uses general negation (لا), which indicates absolute prohibition. The wajh al-dalalah is that the word 'hadd' covers all fixed punishments, and by extension qisas.
4
Distinguish from a related issue
The commentator distinguishes this ruling from a previous discussion about compelling someone to give a surety for the body. Here the issue is voluntarily becoming a surety for the punishment itself, which is still invalid.
5
Conclude the practical consequence
The ruling means that in cases of hadd or qisas, no one can substitute for the criminal. The punishment must be executed on the original offender or be waived (in qisas) by the victim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وكل حق لا يمكن استيفاؤه من الكفيل لا تصح الكفالة به كالحدود والقصاص. (24) ہر وہ حق کہ اس کا وصول کرنا کفیل سے ممکن نہ ہو اس کا کفالہ صحیح نہیں ہے ۔ جیسے حدود اور قصاص۔ جو چیز نفیل سے لینا یا وصول کر ناممکن نہیں اس کا کفیل بنا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ جیسے کوئی کہے کہ مجرم پر اگر حد جاری نہ کر سکو تو میں اس کا کفیل بنتا ہوں کہ مجھ پر وہ حد جاری کر دیں۔ یا مجرم سے قصاص نہ لے سکو تو میں اس کا کفیل بنتا ہوں کہ مجھ سے قصاص لے لو اور میرا ہا تھ قصاص مین کاٹ دو تو یہ کفیل بنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ حدود اور قصاص اصل مجرم سے ہی لئے جاتے ہیں دوسروں سے نہیں۔ اس لئے اس کی کفالت بھی درست نہیں ہیں (۲) حدیث گزر چکی ہے۔ حدثنی عـمـر بـن شعيب عن ابيه عن جده ان النبي الله قال لا كفالة في حد (الف) ( سنن سبیھقی ، باب ماجاء فی الكفالة ببدن من عليه حق ، ج سادس ص ۱۲۷، نمبر ۱۱۴۱۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حد میں کفالت نہیں ہے۔ جس کا ایک مطلب یہ ہے کہ حد کا کوئی کفیل بن جائے کہ مجرم پر نہ کر سکوتو مجھ پر حد جاری کر و تو یہ میچ نہیں ہے۔ وٹ اوپر کے ایک مسئلہ میں تھا کہ حد اور قصاص میں کفالہ بالنفس لینے کے لئے مجبور کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اور یہاں ہے کہ خود حد اور قصاص کا کفیل بننا درست نہیں ہے ۔ اس لئے دونوں مسئلوں میں فرق ہے۔
And every right that cannot be exacted from the surety, the kafalah for it is not valid, like hudud and qisas. (24) Every right that cannot be collected from the surety, its kafalah is not valid, such as hudud and qisas. That which cannot be taken or collected from the surety, it is not valid to become a surety for it. For example, someone says, 'If you cannot execute the hadd on the criminal, then I become surety that you execute that hadd on me;' or 'If you cannot take qisas from the criminal, then I become surety that you take qisas from me and cut my hand in retaliation' — this becoming a surety is not valid. Hudud and qisas are taken from the original criminal, not from others. Therefore, their kafalah is not valid. (2) A hadith has passed: 'Umar ibn Shu'ayb narrated from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) said: 'There is no kafalah in hadd.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-kafalah bi badan man 'alayhi haqq, vol. 6, p. 127, no. 11417) In this hadith, there is no kafalah in hadd. One meaning of this is that no one can become a surety for hadd, that if you cannot execute it on the criminal, then execute it on me — this is not valid. And in a previous issue, it was stated that compelling someone to give a surety for the body in matters of hadd and qisas is not valid. Here, it is that voluntarily becoming a surety for hadd and qisas is not valid. Thus, there is a difference between the two issues.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage establishes a general rule that kafalah is only valid for rights that can be exacted from the surety. Hudud (fixed corporal punishments) and qisas (retaliation) are purely personal to the offender; they cannot be transferred to or executed on a surety. The text provides an example: someone offering to have hadd or qisas carried out on himself if the original criminal is unavailable. This is invalid. A hadith is quoted: 'There is no kafalah in hadd,' which supports the ruling. The commentator distinguishes this from a previous issue about compelling someone to give a surety for the body; here the person volunteers, yet it remains invalid because the punishment is specific to the criminal. The underlying principle is that such rights are not financial and their execution is restricted to the original perpetrator.

Key Terms
حد (hadd): A fixed corporal punishment prescribed by Islamic law, e.g., for theft, adultery.
قصاص (qisas): Retaliation in kind for intentional homicide or injury.
كفالة (kafalah): Suretyship; guaranteeing the debt or appearance of another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is kafalah for hadd invalid even if someone voluntarily offers to be the surety?
A) Because hadd is a financial penalty that cannot be transferred.
B) Because hadd is a right specific to the original criminal; it cannot be executed on a surety.
C) Because the hadd must be carried out in public, and a surety would not be available.
D) Because the hadd is only for men, and women cannot be sureties.

Key Takeaway
Kafalah is invalid for hudud and qisas because these punishments are personal to the offender and cannot be executed on a surety.

Kafalah: When Can You Be a Surety? The Mithl vs 'Ayn Principle
Three rulings on validity of kafalah for price, sale, and hire of a specific animal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi mithl principle to determine the validity of kafalah in contracts of sale and hire.

Core Idea
Kafalah is valid if the surety can pay the like; invalid if exact performance of a specific thing is required.

Kafalah is a contract of guarantee where one person undertakes to fulfill an obligation if the principal debtor fails. However, not all obligations can be guaranteed. The Hanafi school has derived a clear rule: if the obligation is a debt (dayn) that can be paid by an equivalent, kafalah is valid. If it is a specific item (ayn) that must be delivered exactly, kafalah is invalid. In this passage, we examine three practical cases: kafalah for the price (valid), for the sold item (invalid), and for carriage hire with a specific animal (invalid). Through these cases, we understand the underlying principle that the surety's ability to provide the like (mithl) is the key.

Guided Path
1
Identify three scenarios
The text presents three cases: (25) kafalah for the price – valid; (26) kafalah for the sold item – invalid; (27) kafalah for carriage hire with a specific animal – invalid.
2
Extract underlying principle
The validity depends on whether the surety can provide the mithl (like) from his own side. Price is a dayn so mithl suffices; sold item and specific carriage are 'ayn so mithl is insufficient.
The principle is stated explicitly in the Urdu explanation: 'wherever one can give the like from his own side, he can become a surety.'
3
Examine the evidence
The text cites an athar from Ibn 'Umar and a hadith from Bukhari (the man from Bani Isra'il) to support kafalah for a loan/price. These show that suretyship for a financial debt is permissible.
The hadith does not directly mention sale price, but analogy (qiyas) extends the ruling to price as a debt.
4
Apply the principle to new cases
Using the mithl/'ayn distinction, test other contracts. For example, kafalah for a loan (dayn) is valid; kafalah for returning a borrowed specific item ('ariyah) is invalid.
The same principle applies to any obligation where the subject is a specific 'ayn.
